Carrying the Bier: The Sunnah of Haste without Running
States the ruling on how to carry the bier: quickly but not running

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct method of carrying the bier and justify the recommended speed using the two hadiths and the athar.

Core Idea
Carry the bier quickly but never run: the Prophet's guidance balances dignity and haste.

When a Muslim passes away, carrying the janazah to the graveyard is a communal duty. But how should the bier be carried? This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri explains the Sunnah method: hold all four legs, walk briskly without running, and start from the right side. The proofs are drawn from the hadith of Abu Hurairah and Ibn Mas'ud, and the practice of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is carrying the bier. The ruling is that it is Sunnah to hurry but not run, hold all four corners, and start from the right side.
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Two hadith are cited: Bukhari's 'Hurry with the janazah' and Abu Dawud's 'Less than running'. The second qualifies the first.
The imperative 'asri'u' is not a command to run; the other hadith clarifies the intended pace.
3
Examine the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) unless there is evidence of obligation. The phrase 'less than running' provides that evidence, showing the command means quick walking, not running.
Thus, the sunnah is to be brisk, not to run.
4
Confirm the method with athar
Ibn Mas'ud said carrying all sides is Sunnah, and Ibn Umar practiced starting from the right. These support the full method.
5
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school agrees on this ruling; it is not a matter of dispute between the imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۴۲۸] (۲۷) فاذا حملوه على سریره اخذوا بقوائمه الاربع ويمشون به مسرعین دون الخبب

[۴۲۸] (۲۷) پس جب میت کو چار پائی پر اٹھائے تو اس کے چاروں پائیوں کو پکڑے اور اس کو تیزی سے لیکر چلے لیکن دوڑے نہیں ۔ تش میت کو کفن دیگر چار پائی پر لٹائے اور چار پائی کے چاروں پایوں کو پکڑ کر قبرستان کی طرف چلے۔ لیکن اس انداز سے کہ تیزی کے ساتھ قبرستان کی طرف جائے لیکن دوڑے نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ میت کی شان کے خلاف ہے۔ اور میت کے گرنے کا خطرہ ہے۔

جلدی کرنے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الله قال اسرعوا بالجنازة فان تک صالحة فخير تقدمونها وان تک سوى ذلك فشر تضعونهه عن رقابكم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب السرعة بالجنازة ص ۷۶ انمبر ۱۳۱۵)

وفی ابی داؤد، عن ابن مسعود قال سألنا نبينا اللهم عن المشى مع الجنازة فقال مادون الخبب (الف)(ابوداود شریف ، باب الاسراع بالجنازة ج ثانی ص ۹۷ نمبر ۳۱۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنازہ کو تیزی سے قبرستان کی طرف لے جانا چاہئے۔ لیکن دوڑنا نہیں چاہئے ۔ اور چاروں پائے پکڑنے کے لئے یہ اثر ہے قال عبد الله بن مسعود من اتبع جنازة فليحمل بجوانب السرير كلها فانه من السنة (ب) (ابن ماجه شريف، باب ما جاء فی شهودالجنائز ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۷۸۷) اور اثر میں ہے رایت ابن عمر في جنازة فحملوا بجوانب السرير الاربع فبدأ بالميامن ثم تنحى عنها (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۶۸ ، بای جوانب السرير بد آنی العمل ، ج ثانی ص ۴۸۰ نمبر ۱۱۲۷۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چاروں پائوں کو پکڑنا چاہئے۔ اور میت کی دائیں جانب سے پکڑنا شروع کرنا چاہئے۔ الخبب : دوڑنا۔
[428] (27) When they carry him on his bier, they should take hold of its four legs and walk with him quickly without running. [428] (27) So when the deceased is placed on the bier, he should hold its four legs and carry him quickly but not run. ... For hastening there is this hadith from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet: 'Hurry with the janazah; if it is righteous, it is good that you are sending ahead; if otherwise, it is evil that you are putting off your necks.' (Bukhari, chapter on speed with janazah, p. 76, no. 1315). And in Abu Dawud, from Ibn Mas'ud: 'We asked our Prophet about walking with the janazah, and he said: Less than running.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on hastening with janazah, vol. 2, p. 97, no. 3184). From this hadith it is known that the janazah should be taken quickly to the graveyard, but not running. And for holding the four legs, there is this athar: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: Whoever follows a janazah should carry all sides of the bier, for that is from the Sunnah.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on attending janazahs, p. 211, no. 14787). And there is athar: 'I saw Ibn Umar at a janazah: they carried the four sides of the bier, starting with the right side, then moved away.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 480, no. 11277). From this athar it is known that all four legs should be held, and one should start from the right side. Al-khabab: running.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on how the bier should be carried. The matn states: when they carry him on his bier, they take hold of its four legs and walk quickly without running. The Urdu commentary explains that one should hold all four legs of the bier and proceed quickly to the graveyard but not run, as that is against the dignity of the deceased and risks dropping the bier. The proof for hurrying is the hadith in Bukhari: 'Hurry with the janazah...' and the hadith in Abu Dawud where the Prophet said to walk 'less than running' (madoona al-khabab). The method of holding all four corners is supported by the athar of Ibn Mas'ud (that it is Sunnah) and the practice of Ibn Umar who started from the right side. Thus, the proper way is: carry the bier on the shoulders, holding all four legs, walk briskly but not run, and begin from the right side.

Key Terms
الخبب (al-khabab): Running; specifically a fast pace between walking and running.
سرير (sareer): Bier; the stretcher on which the deceased is carried.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this passage, what is the recommended speed for carrying the janazah?
A) Walking slowly
B) Running fast
C) Walking quickly but not running
D) Jogging

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah is to carry the bier quickly without running, holding all four legs and starting from the right, as proven by hadith and the practice of the sahabah.

Sitting Before the Bier is Placed
States ruling on sitting before bier placed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting before the bier is placed and identify the proof from athar.

Core Idea
Sitting before the bier is placed is makruh, not haram — necessity permits it.

This lesson covers the etiquette of attending a janazah at the graveside. The matn states it is disliked to sit before the carriers place the bier. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: respect for the deceased and the carriers' need for assistance. A narrated athar provides the proof. We will explore the ruling, its evidence, and the exception for necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sitting before the bier is placed from the carriers' shoulders. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
The Arabic says 'kariha' which in Hanafi usul indicates dislike, not prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar from Abu Hurairah and Abu Sa'id: 'When you are at a janazah, do not sit until the bier is placed.'
This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la tajlisu' (do not sit) is a prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition from a non-mutawatir source indicates karahah (dislike), not tahrim (unlawfulness).
The transmission (thubut) is zanni, so the highest level it can command is karahah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may consider sitting permissible without dislike. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh but allowed if necessary.
The text mentions necessity as an exception.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is makruh, but sitting is permissible when there is a genuine need (e.g., illness, inability to stand).
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۲۹ (۲۸) فاذا بلغوا الی قبره کره للناس ان يجلسوا قبل ان يوضع من اعناق الرجال

[۴۲۹] (۲۸) پس جب قبر تک پہنچ جائے تو لوگوں کے لئے مکروہ ہے کہ بیٹھے مردوں کے گردنوں سے رکھنے سے پہلے۔ ابھی میت کو اٹھانے والوں نے اپنے کندھے سے زمین پر رکھا نہیں ہے اس سے پہلے عام لوگ بیٹھ جائیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ (۱) یہ میت کی شان کے خلاف ہے (۲) اٹھانے والوں کو ضرورت پڑ سکتی ہے کہ چار پائی کو پکڑے ۔ اس لئے میت کو رکھنے سے پہلے عام لوگوں کو نہیں بیٹھنا چاہئے۔ البتہ مجبوری ہوتو بیٹھ سکتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابی هریرة انه لم يكن يقعد حتى يوضع السرير ، و عن ابي سعيد قال اذا كنتم في جنازة فلا تجلسوا حتى يوضع السرير (و) (مصنف ابن ابی شیۃ 99، فی الرجل يكون مع الجنازة من قال لا تجلس حتی یوضع ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳، نمبر ۱۱۵۱۱/۱۱۵۱۰) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنازہ کے رکھنے سے پہلے نہیں بیٹھنا چاہئے۔
[429] (28) When they reach his grave, it is disliked for people to sit before it is placed down from the necks of the men. [429] (28) So when they reach the grave, it is makruh for people to sit before the deceased is placed from the shoulders (of the carriers). The carriers have not yet put it down from their shoulders to the ground; before that, if common people sit, it is makruh. (1) This is against the dignity of the deceased. (2) The carriers may need to hold the bier. Therefore, before placing the deceased, common people should not sit. However, if there is a necessity, one may sit. The proof for this is the athar from Abu Hurairah that he would not sit until the bier was placed, and from Abu Sa'id: 'When you are at a janazah, do not sit until the bier is placed.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 3, p. 13, nos. 11511/11510). From this it is known that one should not sit before the janazah is placed.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the etiquette of attending a janazah at the graveside. The matn states that it is disliked (makruh) for people to sit before the bier is placed from the necks of the men (i.e., before the carriers set it down). The Urdu commentary explains two reasons: first, sitting before the bier is placed is contrary to the dignity of the deceased; second, the carriers may need assistance in holding the bier. However, if there is a genuine necessity (like illness or inability to stand), one may sit. The proof is from the practice of Abu Hurairah and the explicit saying of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'Do not sit until the bier is placed.' This is a narrated athar that establishes the disliked nature of premature sitting.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action that is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Always
D) Only for the carriers

Key Takeaway
Sitting before the bier is placed is makruh, but necessity allows it — respect for the deceased takes priority.

Digging the Grave: Lahd and Shaqq
States the ruling on grave construction and the two permissible methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two permissible types of grave construction in the Hanafi school and identify which is recommended.

Core Idea
Both lahd and shaqq are valid, but lahd is the sunnah when soil permits.

When preparing a grave for burial, the Hanafi school prescribes two methods: lahd (a side niche) and shaqq (a deep trench). This lesson explains the ruling, the conditions for each, and the preferred practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is constructing the grave. The text states that a lahd should be made, but then elaborates that both lahd and shaqq are permissible.
The primary instruction is lahd, but the commentary expands.
2
Distinguish the two types
Lahd: a vertical pit with a side niche. Shaqq: a deep trench covered with wood. Know the difference in construction.
3
Note the condition for each
Lahd is used when soil is firm; shaqq is used when soil is loose. The grave-digger assesses the soil.
The condition is based on practicality, not ritual.
4
Determine the preference
Lahd is better (afdal) and more economical. It is the sunnah method. Shaqq is a permissible alternative.
The hukm level for lahd is sunnah muakkadah; for shaqq it is mubah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۰] (۲۹) قبر کھودی جائے اور لحد بنائی جائے۔

ر قبر دو طرح سے کھودی جاتی ہے۔ ایک لحد یعنی سیدھی کھود کر پھر دائیں جانب کنارہ کھود کر میت کو رکھنے کی جگہ بنائی جائے اور اس میں میت کو رکھ کر کنارہ پر کچی اینٹ رکھ دی جائے۔ اور دوسری شکل شق کی ہے یعنی سیدھی کھودی جائے اور گہرا کر کے اس میں میت کو رکھا جائے اور اوپر سے لکڑی ڈال کر پاٹ دی جائے۔ دونوں قسم جائز ہے۔ اور مٹی حالت دیکھ کر قبر کھودی جاتی ہے۔ البتہ لحد زیادہ بہتر ہے اور اس میں خرچ
[430] (29) The grave should be dug and a lahd made. The grave is dug in two ways. One is lahd: dig straight down, then dig a niche on the right side to place the deceased, then place the deceased and close the niche with unbaked bricks. The second form is shaqq: dig straight down deep, place the deceased inside, then place wood over and cover it. Both types are permissible. The grave is dug according to the condition of the soil. However, lahd is better and more economical.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the construction of graves. The matn states: 'ويحفر قبر ويحد له' meaning the grave should be dug and a lahd (niche) should be made. The Urdu commentary explains two types: lahd and shaqq. In lahd, the grave is dug vertically, and then a horizontal niche is dug on the qibla side (right side) to place the body; the niche is then sealed with unbaked bricks to prevent soil from falling on the body. In shaqq, a deep trench is dug, the body is placed inside, and then the grave is covered with wooden planks or similar material. Both methods are permissible (ja'iz). The choice depends on the soil: lahd is preferred if the soil is firm enough; if it is loose, shaqq is used. Lahd is considered better (afdal) and also less costly. This reflects the Hanafi position that lahd is the sunnah method.

Key Terms
لحد (lahd): A niche dug sideways from the bottom of the grave to place the deceased.
شق (shaqq): A straight trench dug deep and covered with wood or stone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of grave is recommended?
A) Shaqq only
B) Lahd only
C) Both lahd and shaqq are permissible, but lahd is better
D) Neither; the grave should be made without any niche

Key Takeaway
Both lahd and shaqq are permissible; lahd is recommended when soil is firm.

Carrying the Bier and Walking Speed: The Sunnah Method
Ruling with proof on carrying the bier and walking speed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sunnah method of carrying the bier and the recommended walking speed, and identify the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Carry the bier from all four sides, starting right, and walk briskly without running.

This lesson covers the proper manner of transporting the deceased to the grave. The Hanafi school derives the method from specific narrations: the bier should be held by its four legs and walked briskly, but not run. These actions are Sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory, and their proofs come from the Prophet's guidance and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two key acts: (1) carrying the bier by its four legs, and (2) walking briskly without running (al-khabab). Both are ruled as Sunnah.
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Examine the hadith evidence for each
For walking speed: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud states 'less than running' (mā dūna al-khabab). For carrying by four sides: the athar of Ibn Mas'ud and the practice of Ibn Umar are cited.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the ruling is still acted upon.
3
Understand the status: Sunnah, not wajib
The Hanafi position box confirms the rulings are Sunnah muakkadah. Missing them does not invalidate the funeral, but following them is meritorious.
4
Note the practical procedure
Carrying should begin from the right side of the deceased, and all four sides should be used. The walk should be faster than normal but not a run.
The bier is carried on the shoulders, and four people each hold one leg.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سریره اخذوا بقوائمه الاربع ويمشون به مسرعین دون الخبب [۴۲۹ (۲۸) فاذا بلغوا الی قبره کره للناس ان يجلسوا قبل ان يوضع من اعناق الرجال [۴۳۰](۲۹) ويحفر القبر ويلحد [۴۳۱] (۳۰) ويدخل الميت مما يلى القبلة [۴۳۲ (۳۱) فاذا وضع في لحده قال الذى يضعه بسم الله و على ملة رسول الله [۴۳۳](۳۲) ويوجهه الى
وفی ابی داؤد، عن ابن مسعود قال سألنا نبينا اللهم عن المشى مع الجنازة فقال مادون الخبب (الف)(ابوداود شریف ، باب الاسراع بالجنازة ج ثانی ص ۹۷ نمبر ۳۱۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنازہ کو تیزی سے قبرستان کی طرف لے جانا چاہئے۔ لیکن دوڑنا نہیں چاہئے ۔ اور چاروں پائے پکڑنے کے لئے یہ اثر ہے قال عبد الله بن مسعود من اتبع جنازة فليحمل بجوانب السرير كلها فانه من السنة (ب) (ابن ماجه شريف، باب ما جاء فی شهودالجنائز ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۷۸۷) اور اثر میں ہے رایت ابن عمر في جنازة فحملوا بجوانب السرير الاربع فبدأ بالميامن ثم تنحى عنها (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۶۸ ، بای جوانب السرير بد آنی العمل ، ج ثانی ص ۴۸۰ نمبر ۱۱۲۷۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چاروں پائوں کو پکڑنا چاہئے۔ اور میت کی دائیں جانب سے پکڑنا شروع کرنا چاہئے۔ الخبب : دوڑنا۔
His bier: they take it by its four legs and walk with it briskly without running. [429 (28) When they reach his grave, it is disliked for people to sit before it is placed from the necks of the men. [430](29) And they dig the grave and make a niche. [431] (30) And they enter the deceased from the direction of the qibla. [432 (31) When he is placed in his niche, the one who places him says: Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah. [433](32) And they face him towards the qibla. And in Abu Dawud, from Ibn Mas'ud: We asked our Prophet about walking with the funeral, and he said: Less than running. (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on hastening with the funeral, vol. 2, p. 97, no. 3184) From this hadith it is known that the funeral should be taken quickly to the cemetery, but not running. And for holding the four legs, there is this narration: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: Whoever follows a funeral, then let him carry from all sides of the bier, for it is from the Sunnah. (b) (Ibn Majah, chapter on witnessing funerals, p. 211, no. 14787) And there is a narration: I saw Ibn 'Umar at a funeral, and they carried from all four sides of the bier, beginning with the right side, then he moved away from it. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 68, bab jawamb al-sarir, vol. 2, p. 480, no. 11277) From this narration it is known that all four legs should be held, and one should begin from the right side of the deceased. Al-khabab: running.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that the bier should be carried by its four legs and walked briskly, without running. The proofs are from hadith: the Prophet specified walking less than running (mā dūna al-khabab). It also cites that carrying from all four sides is Sunnah, and the right side should be started with.

Key Terms
السرير (al-sarīr): The bier or stretcher upon which the deceased is carried.
الخبب (al-khabab): Running or a fast gait; the text says 'without al-khabab' meaning a brisk walk, not running.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By two persons on the right side only
B) By four persons, each holding one leg, starting from the right side
C) By one person dragging it
D) By throwing it over shoulders

Key Takeaway
Carry the bier from all four sides, starting from the right, and walk briskly without running – these are emphasized Sunnah acts in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Sitting Before the Bier is Placed
Ruling with proof on sitting before bier placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting before the bier is placed and identify the evidence from the practice of the Companions and a hadith.

Core Idea
It is disliked (makruh tanzih) to sit before the bier is placed from the carriers' shoulders, but necessity allows it.

This passage addresses a specific etiquette in funeral processions: whether one may sit before the bier is set down at the grave. The text clarifies that it is disliked (makruh) to sit prematurely, citing the dignity of the deceased and the practical needs of the carriers. The ruling is based on the practice of Abu Hurairah and a hadith from Abu Sa'id.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sitting before the bier is placed from the carriers' shoulders. The ruling is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked).
Distinguish between makruh tanzih and tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: the practice of Abu Hurairah (he would not sit until the bier was placed) and a hadith from Abu Sa'id: 'When you are at a funeral, do not sit until the bier is placed.'
The hadith is reported in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition 'لا تجلسوا' (do not sit) indicates dislike (karahah) according to Hanafi usul, as a prohibition does not necessarily imply tahrim (forbidden) without additional evidence.
Hanafis interpret nahy as karahah unless there is a qarinah for tahrim.
4
Note the exceptions
The text mentions that necessity (darurah) permits sitting. This aligns with the general principle that necessity overrides prohibitions (al-darurah tubih al-mahzurat).
This exception prevents undue hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۲۹] (۲۸) فاذا بلغوا الی قبره کره للناس ان يجلسوا قبل ان يوضع من اعناق الرجال [۴۳۰](۲۹) ويحفر القبر ويلحد
پس جب قبر تک پہنچ جائے تو لوگوں کے لئے مکروہ ہے کہ بیٹھے مردوں کے گردنوں سے رکھنے سے پہلے۔ ابھی میت کو اٹھانے والوں نے اپنے کندھے سے زمین پر رکھا نہیں ہے اس سے پہلے عام لوگ بیٹھ جائیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ (۱) یہ میت کی شان کے خلاف ہے (۲) اٹھانے والوں کو ضرورت پڑ سکتی ہے کہ چار پائی کو پکڑے ۔ اس لئے میت کو رکھنے سے پہلے عام لوگوں کو نہیں بیٹھنا چاہئے۔ البتہ مجبوری ہوتو بیٹھ سکتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابی هریرة انه لم يكن يقعد حتى يوضع السرير ، و عن ابي سعيد قال اذا كنتم في جنازة فلا تجلسوا حتى يوضع السرير (و) (مصنف ابن ابی شیۃ 99، فی الرجل يكون مع الجنازة من قال لا تجلس حتی یوضع ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳، نمبر ۱۱۵۱۱/۱۱۵۱۰) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنازہ کے رکھنے سے پہلے نہیں بیٹھنا چاہئے۔
[429] (28) When they reach his grave, it is disliked for people to sit before it is placed from the necks of the men. [430](29) And they dig the grave and make a niche. So when they reach the grave, it is disliked for people to sit before placing from the necks of the carriers. The carriers have not yet placed the deceased from their shoulders to the ground; before that, for common people to sit is disliked. (1) It is against the dignity of the deceased. (2) The carriers might need to hold the bier. Therefore, common people should not sit before the deceased is placed. However, if there is a necessity, one may sit. The proof is this narration: From Abu Hurairah that he would not sit until the bier was placed, and from Abu Sa'id who said: When you are at a funeral, do not sit until the bier is placed. (d) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 99, etc.) From this it is known that one should not sit before the bier is placed.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof: it is makruh (disliked) for people to sit before the bier is placed from the carriers' necks. The reasons given are: it goes against the dignity of the deceased, and the carriers may need assistance. The proof is from the practice of Abu Hurairah and a hadith from Abu Sa'id. Necessity may allow sitting.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; the Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) rather than haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) During the funeral prayer
B) Before the bier is placed from the carriers' shoulders
C) After the burial
D) While carrying the bier

Key Takeaway
It is disliked to sit before the bier is placed at the grave, but necessity makes it permissible.

Lahd vs Shaq: The Sunnah Method of Grave Digging
Ruling on grave digging methods with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between lahd and shaq, state the Hanafi ruling (lahd is Sunnah muakkadah, shaq is permissible), and cite the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
Lahd is the Sunnah for grave digging, but shaq is permissible when needed.

When preparing a grave, the Hanafi school recognises two methods: lahd (a niche dug sideways toward the qibla) and shaq (a straight trench). While both are valid, the Prophet ﷺ himself was buried in a lahd, and his practice establishes it as the preferred Sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical circumstances that may justify using shaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two grave types
Read the description of lahd and shaq. Note the key difference: lahd has a side niche, shaq is a straight cut.
2
State the hukm for each
From the text, both are permissible (ja'iz), but lahd is 'better' (afdal) and Sunnah. Confirm that shaq is allowed when needed, e.g., loose soil.
3
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: (1) Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas' instruction to make a lahd for him, following the Prophet's burial; (2) The Prophet's statement 'Lahd is for us, shaq is for others.' Identify the sources (Muslim, Tirmidhi).
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith shows the Prophet's practice (fi'l), which indicates sunniyyah. The second hadith explicitly distinguishes 'us' (the Muslims) from 'others', making lahd a distinctive Sunnah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may prefer shaq in certain regions. The Hanafi preference for lahd is based on these ahadith and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۰] (۲۹) قبر کھودی جائے اور لحد بنائی جائے۔
ر قبر دو طرح سے کھودی جاتی ہے۔ ایک لحد یعنی سیدھی کھود کر پھر دائیں جانب کنارہ کھود کر میت کو رکھنے کی جگہ بنائی جائے اور اس میں میت کو رکھ کر کنارہ پر کچی اینٹ رکھ دی جائے۔ اور دوسری شکل شق کی ہے یعنی سیدھی کھودی جائے اور گہرا کر کے اس میں میت کو رکھا جائے اور اوپر سے لکڑی ڈال کر پاٹ دی جائے۔ دونوں قسم جائز ہے۔ اور مٹی حالت دیکھ کر قبر کھودی جاتی ہے۔ البتہ لحد زیادہ بہتر ہے اور اس میں خرچ بھی کم ہے۔ لحد مسنون ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے ان سعد بن وقاص قال في مرضه الذي هلك فيه الحدوا لي لحدا وانصبوا على اللبن نصبا كما صنع برسول الله الله الف) (مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل فی استحباب اللحد ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۹۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لحد زیادہ بہتر ہے اور سنت ہے (۲) ترندی میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اللحد لنا والشق لغيرنا (ب) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی قول النبي اللحد لنا و الشق لغیر نا ص ۱۳۰۳ نمبر ۰۴۵ ارابو داؤد شریف، باب فی اللحد ج خانی ص ۱۰۲ نمبر (۳۲۰۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ لحد مسنون ہے۔
[430] (29) The grave is dug and a niche is made. The grave is dug in two ways: one is lahd – that is, they dig straight then on the right side they dig a ledge to make a place for the deceased, place the deceased in it, and put unbaked bricks on the ledge. The other form is shaq – that is, they dig straight and deeper, place the deceased in it, and cover with wood and earth. Both types are permissible. The digging depends on the soil condition. However, lahd is better and less expensive. The reason lahd is Sunnah is this hadith: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Make a lahd for me and set up bricks over me as was done for the Messenger of Allah.' (a) (Muslim, Kitab al-Jana'iz, chapter on istihbab al-lahd, p. 311, no. 966) From this hadith it is known that lahd is better and Sunnah. (2) In Tirmidhi, from Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet said: 'Lahd is for us, and shaq is for others.' (b) (Tirmidhi, chapter on the Prophet's saying 'lahd is for us and shaq for others', p. 1303, no. 045; and Abu Dawud, chapter on lahd, vol. 2, p. 102, no. 3208) From this hadith it is also known that lahd is Sunnah.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on grave digging. Two forms are described: lahd (niche dug sideways from the bottom) and shaq (excavation straight down). Both are permissible, but lahd is better and Sunnah, as proven by hadith from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and the Prophet's statement 'Lahd is for us, shaq for others.' The choice depends on soil; if soil is loose, shaq may be used.

Key Terms
اللحد (al-lahd): A niche dug sideways at the bottom of the grave, toward the qibla, to place the deceased.
الشق (al-shaq): An excavation dug straight down, like a trench, in which the deceased is placed and covered with wood or slabs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram because it contradicts the Sunnah.
B) It is makruh tanzihi and should be avoided.
C) It is permissible (ja'iz) and may be used when lahd is impractical.
D) It is wajib in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Lahd is the confirmed Sunnah for grave digging, but shaq is a valid permissible alternative when needed.

Entering the Deceased from the Qibla Side: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on entering the deceased from the qibla side with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on entering the deceased into the grave, compare it with the Shafi'i view, and identify the proofs used by each school.

Core Idea
The deceased should be entered from the qibla side — a mustahabb act supported by the Prophet's practice.

When burying the deceased, one of the actions is how to position the body for placement in the grave. The Hanafi school recommends a specific side, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. This lesson examines the Hanafi view and the opposing Shafi'i view, along with their respective proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the recommended method: entering the deceased from the side of the grave that faces the qibla. This is considered mustahabb.
The term 'mimmā yalī al-qiblah' means from the direction of the qibla.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the deceased should be entered from the foot end of the grave.
The foot end is opposite the qibla side.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on a narration from 'Abdullah ibn Yazid who entered Al-Harith from the foot end and stated 'This is from the Sunnah' (Abu Dawud).
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on a hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: the Prophet entered a grave at night and took the deceased from the qibla side (Tirmidhi).
This hadith is explicit about the Prophet's action.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is which side of the grave the person lowering the body stands: Hanafis stand at the qibla side; Shafi'is stand at the foot end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۱] (۳۰) ويدخل الميت مما يلى القبلة [۴۳۲ (۳۱) فاذا وضع في لحده قال الذى يضعه بسم الله و على ملة رسول الله [۴۳۳](۳۲) ويوجهه الى
[۴۳۱] (۳۰) میت کو قبلہ کی جانب سے داخل کیا جائے۔
میت کو قبر میں داخل کرنے کی دو شکلیں ہیں (۱) یہ کہ میت کو قبر کے قبلہ کی جانب رکھی جائے اور وہاں سے قبر میں داخل کرے ۔ یہی حنفیہ کے یہاں مستحب ہے۔ اور دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ میت کو قبر کی پاتانے کی طرف رکھی جائے اور وہاں سے سر کا کر قبر میں داخل کیا جائے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبي دخل قبرا ليلا فاسرج لى سراج فاخذه من قبل القبلة (ج) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الدفن باللیل ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۷ ۱۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کی جانب سے میت کو قبر میں داخل کیا جائے۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک پاتانے کی جانب سے میت کو ڈالا جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابی اسحاق قال اوصى الحارث ان يصلى عليه عبد الله بن يزيد فصلى عليه ثم ادخله القبر من قبل رجلى القبر وقال هذا من السنة (و) (ابوداؤد شريف ، باب کیف یدخل المیت قبرہ ص ۱۰۲ نمبر ۳۱۲۱۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کی جانب سے داخل کیا جائے۔
[431] (30) And they enter the deceased from the direction of the qibla. [432 (31) When he is placed in his niche, the one who places him says: Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah. [433](32) And they face him towards. [431] (30) The deceased is entered from the qibla side. There are two methods of entering the deceased into the grave: (1) The deceased is placed at the qibla side of the grave and entered from there. This is mustahabb (recommended) according to the Hanafis. The other method is that the deceased is placed at the foot end of the grave and entered from there head first. From Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet entered a grave at night, a lamp was lit for him, and he took the deceased from the qibla side. (c) (Tirmidhi, chapter on burial at night, p. 204, no. 105) From this hadith it is known that the deceased should be entered from the qibla side. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the deceased should be entered from the foot end. His proof is this narration: From Abu Ishaq: Al-Harith willed that 'Abdullah ibn Yazid should pray over him, so he prayed and then entered him into the grave from the foot end of the grave, and said: This is from the Sunnah. (d) (Abu Dawud, chapter on how to enter the deceased into the grave, p. 102, no. 31211) From this narration it is known that he should be entered from the foot end.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school recommends entering the deceased from the qibla side, based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about the Prophet's action. The Shafi'i school prefers entering from the foot end (leg side), based on the practice of 'Abdullah ibn Yazid and Al-Harith. The text presents both positions without explicit tarjih, but the Hanafi position is given first as mustahabb.

Key Terms
مما يلى القبلة (mimmā yalī al-qiblah): From the direction of the qibla; entering the deceased from the side of the grave that faces the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The practice of 'Abdullah ibn Yazid
B) The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about the Prophet
C) The Quranic verse on burial
D) Consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends entering the deceased from the qibla side based on the Prophet's practice, while the Shafi'i school prefers the foot end; both sides have valid evidence, but the Hanafi position is mustahabb.

The Sunnah Phrase When Placing the Deceased in the Grave
Ruling on what to say when placing the deceased in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sunnah phrase to recite when placing the deceased in the grave and identify the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
When placing the deceased, say 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah' — a confirmed Sunnah of the Prophet.

This lesson covers a brief but meaningful act of the funeral rites: the words recited when lowering the deceased into the grave. Though small, it reflects the Sunna of the Prophet ﷺ and connects the deceased to the milla of Islam. The Hanafi school teaches this as a recommended practice with clear prophetic precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting a specific phrase when placing the deceased in the grave. The ruling is Sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet regularly did it and encouraged it, but omitting it does not invalidate the burial.
2
Locate the dalil and examine its wording
The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said various phrasings: 'Bismillah wa billahi wa 'ala millati Rasulillah' and 'Bismillah wa 'ala sunnati Rasulillah.'
The hadith is narrated by Tirmidhi (1046) and Abu Dawud (3213).
3
Note the variance in wording
The Prophet used more than one phrasing, showing flexibility. The preferred wording in the Hanafi school is 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah,' but other variants are permissible.
Variance indicates the sunnah is in the general meaning, not a rigid formula.
4
Conclude with the preferred Hanafi practice
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to say 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah.' This is the practice recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah and is followed by the majority.
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this matter.

This is a ruling with proof. When placing the deceased in the grave, the person doing so should say 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah' or variant expressions as reported from the Prophet. The hadith is clear that this is a Sunnah practice.

بسم الله و على ملة رسول الله (Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah): The phrase recited when placing the deceased in the grave, meaning 'In the name of Allah and on the religion of the Messenger of Allah.'

Facing the Deceased Towards the Qibla
Ruling on turning the deceased's face towards the qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the direction of the deceased in the grave and identify the sunnah manner of placement.

Core Idea
Turn the deceased's face to the qibla — it is a confirmed sunnah.

In burials, we follow the sunnah of the Prophet. A key element is orienting the deceased's face towards the qibla. This brief ruling from the matn establishes the practice. Let us explore its status and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is turning the deceased's face towards the qibla when placing them in the grave. The ruling is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the Hanafi school.
This is not fard or wajib; its omission does not invalidate the burial.
2
Understand the Basis (Dalil)
The evidence comes from the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Sahaba. The hadith references in the footnote (though covering other topics) confirm that these details are Sunnah.
The Hanafi school relies on the established practice (sunnah 'amaliyyah) of the early Muslims.
3
Determine the Manner
The deceased is laid on his or her right side, with the face directly towards the qibla. This ensures the entire body is aligned.
Some mistakenly place the deceased on their back; the sunnah is on the side.
4
Consider the Practical Application
When digging the grave, a niche (lahd) is made on the qibla side, and the body is laid in it facing qibla. If a lah is not possible, the body is placed normally with the face turned.
This ruling is universally agreed upon among the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۳] (۳۲) ويوجهه الى القبلة
[۴۳۳] (۳۲) اور میت کا چہرہ قبلہ کی طرف پھیر دے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور گو جنازہ کے ساتھ چلنے کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا دوڑنے سے تھوڑا کم ( لے کر چلو ) (ب) عبداللہ بن مسعود نے فرمایا جو جنازہ کے پیچھے چلے تو چار پائی کے چاروں جانب اٹھائے اس لئے کہ وہ سنت ہے (ج) حضرت ابن عمر کو جنازہ میں دیکھا کہ وہ چار پائی کے چاروں جانب اٹھاتے تھے اور دائیں جانب سے شروع کرتے پھر اس سے الگ ہو جاتے (د) ابو ہریرہ سے منقول ہے کہ وہ نہیں بیٹھتے تھے یہاں تک کہ چار پائی رکھی جائے۔ اور ابوسعید سے منقول ہے کہ فرمایا کہ جب تم جنازہ میں ہو تو مت بیٹھو جب تک کہ چار پائی نہ رکھی جائے۔

Footnote: (a) I asked our Prophet about walking with the funeral, and he said: Less than running. (c) I saw Ibn 'Umar at a funeral, and they carried from all four sides of the bier, beginning with the right side, then he moved away. (d) From Abu Hurairah that he would not sit until the bier was placed, and from Abu Sa'id who said: When you are at a funeral, do not sit until the bier is placed.

Commentary
This is a brief ruling: the deceased's face should be turned towards the qibla when placed in the grave. The text does not provide an explicit proof here; the footnote collects the hadith used in previous rulings. The ruling is consistent with general Hanafi practice that the deceased is laid on his right side facing qibla.

Key Terms
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction of prayer (the Kaaba) towards which the deceased's face is turned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Wajib
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Facing the deceased towards the qibla is a confirmed sunnah of burial, done by laying the body on its right side with the face directed to the qibla.

Entering the Deceased from the Qibla Side
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on entering the grave from the qibla side.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the deceased into the grave, provide the Hanafi proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds it mustahabb to enter the deceased from the qibla side, based on a hadith of Ibn Abbas.

This lesson examines a specific difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding funeral rites. While the ruling is not obligatory, understanding the proof and the practical difference helps appreciate how madhahib approach a common act of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school considers it mustahabb (recommended) to enter the deceased from the side facing the qibla.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the deceased should be entered from the foot end of the grave.
This is considered sunnah in the Shafi'i school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is an athar from Abu Ishaq: Al-Harith's will that Abdullah bin Yazid pray over him and then enter him from the foot side, declaring it sunnah.
Source: Abu Dawood
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is not explicitly given in this passage, but the Hanafi position is presented as relied-upon based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
The commentator does not refute the Shafi'i proof, only presents the Hanafi view as mustahabb.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the direction from which the body is lowered into the grave: from the qibla side (Hanafi) vs. from the foot end (Shafi'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۱] (۳۰) میت کو قبلہ کی جانب سے داخل کیا جائے۔

میت کو قبر میں داخل کرنے کی دو شکلیں ہیں (۱) یہ کہ میت کو قبر کے قبلہ کی جانب رکھی جائے اور وہاں سے قبر میں داخل کرے ۔ یہی حنفیہ کے یہاں مستحب ہے۔ اور دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ میت کو قبر کی پاتانے کی طرف رکھی جائے اور وہاں سے سر کا کر قبر میں داخل کیا جائے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبي دخل قبرا ليلا فاسرج لى سراج فاخذه من قبل القبلة (ج) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الدفن باللیل ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۷ ۱۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کی جانب سے میت کو قبر میں داخل کیا جائے۔

امام شافعی کے نزدیک پاتانے کی جانب سے میت کو ڈالا جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابی اسحاق قال اوصى الحارث ان يصلى عليه عبد الله بن يزيد فصلى عليه ثم ادخله القبر من قبل رجلى القبر وقال هذا من السنة (و) (ابوداؤد شريف ، باب کیف یدخل المیت قبرہ ص ۱۰۲ نمبر ۳۱۲۱۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پاؤں کی جانب سے داخل کیا جائے۔
[431] (30) The deceased should be entered from the side facing the qibla.

There are two ways of entering the deceased into the grave: (1) The deceased is placed on the side of the grave facing the qibla and entered from there. This is mustahabb in the Hanafi school. The second way is that the deceased is placed at the foot end of the grave and entered from there head first. From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet entered a grave at night, so a lamp was lit for him, and he took the deceased from the direction of the qibla. (Hadith from Tirmidhi, chapter on burial at night) This hadith shows that the deceased should be entered from the qibla side.

According to Imam Shafi'i, the deceased should be placed from the foot side. His proof is the athar from Abu Ishaq who said Al-Harith willed that Abdullah bin Yazid pray over him, so he prayed over him, then entered him into the grave from the side of the feet and said, 'This is the Sunnah.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on how to enter the deceased into the grave) This athar shows that entry should be from the foot side.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the direction from which the deceased should be entered into the grave. The passage begins by stating the ruling (30) that the deceased should be entered from the side of the qibla. The Hanafi commentator then explains the two methods: the Hanafi preferred method (mustahabb) is to place the deceased on the qibla side of the grave and enter from there, while the other method (associated with Shafi'i) is to place the deceased at the foot of the grave and enter head first. The Hanafi proof is a hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet entered a grave at night and took the deceased from the qibla side. Then the Shafi'i position is presented: they hold that entry should be from the foot end, based on an athar from Al-Harith's funeral where Abdullah bin Yazid entered the grave from the foot side and declared it sunnah. The commentary does not explicitly provide a Hanafi response, but the Hanafi position is presented as the preferred view.

Key Terms
قبلہ (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, towards which Muslims pray and face the deceased in the grave.
مستحب (mustahabb): An action that is recommended but not obligatory; its omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, from which direction should the deceased be entered into the grave?
A) From the foot end of the grave
B) From the side of the qibla
C) From any direction
D) From the head end

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends entering the deceased from the qibla side, while the Shafi'i school recommends from the foot end; both are based on narrations.

Turning the Deceased Towards the Qibla: Sunnah with Evidence
Ruling with proof on facing the deceased towards the qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm level of turning the deceased towards the qibla and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The qibla is for the living and the dead — turning the deceased towards it is a confirmed sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on positioning the deceased towards the qibla. The Hanafi school considers this a sunnah mu'akkadah, supported by a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ refers to the Kaaba as the qibla for both living and dead. Understanding this ruling helps us fulfill the rights of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
What exactly is being ruled upon (turning the face of the deceased towards qibla) and what is its classification (sunnah mu'akkadah)?
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Find the specific hadith quoted, its source (Abu Dawood, Bayhaqi), and note that it is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the phrase 'qiblatakum ahya'an wa amwatan' prove that the deceased should face the qibla?
4
Confirm the authority and hukm rationale
Why does the Hanafi school classify this as sunnah rather than wajib? Because the dalil is zanni in both transmission and meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۳] (۳۲) اور میت کا چہرہ قبلہ کی طرف پھیر دے۔

زندگی میں قبلہ کی طرف نماز پڑھتا رہا اب موت کے بعد بھی قبلہ ہی کی طرف چہرہ ہو (۲) ان رجلا سأله فقال يا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما الكبائر ؟ قال من تسع فذكر معناه وزاد وعقوق الوالدين المسلمين واستحلال البيت الحرام قبلتكم احياء و امواتا (الف) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی التشديد في اكل مال الیتیم ج ثانی ص ۴۱ نمبر ۲۸۷۵ رسنن سبیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی استقبال القبلة بالموتی ج ثالث ص ۵۷۳ نمبر ۶۷۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کو بھی قبلہ کی طرف لٹایا جائے۔
[433] (32) And turn his face towards the qibla.

He used to pray towards the qibla in life, so after death his face should also be towards the qibla. (2) A man asked him: 'O Messenger of Allah, what are the major sins?' He said: 'Nine' and mentioned their meanings, and added 'disobeying Muslim parents and treating the Sacred House as permissible, which is your qibla, living and dead.' (Abu Dawood and Bayhaqi) This hadith shows that the deceased should also be laid facing the qibla.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that the face of the deceased should be turned towards the qibla. The commentary provides a rationale: just as the person prayed facing the qibla in life, so after death he should face it. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet mentions the Sacred House as the qibla for both the living and the dead, indicating that the deceased should be oriented towards it. This ruling is consistent across schools.

Key Terms
قبلہ (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that turning the deceased towards the qibla is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), supported by the hadith that the Kaaba is the qibla for the living and the dead.

Untying the Knots of the Shroud
Ruling with proof on untying shroud knots.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on untying the knots of the shroud after burial and identify the evidence from the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
Untying the shroud knots after burial is a recommended (sunnah) practice, not obligatory.

When preparing a deceased for burial, the shroud is often tied to keep it secure. After the body is placed in the grave, the Hanafi school follows the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i in recommending that these knots be undone. This lesson explains the ruling and its proof from early Muslim practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level?
The act is untying the knots after burial; the ruling is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? How is it transmitted?
The evidence is an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the athar directly support the ruling?
The explicit instruction to 'untie all the knots' indicates the recommended practice.
4
Note the authority level
Is this from Zahir al-Riwayah or Nawadir?
This is from the Nawadir (rare transmissions), but it is accepted practice.
5
State the mufta bihi
What is the operative ruling for practice today?
It is recommended to untie the knots after burial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۴] (۳۳) گرہ کھول دے۔ کفن دیتے وقت کھلنے کا خطرہ ہو تو گرہ لگانے کے لئے کہا تھا۔ اب قبر میں میت کو لٹانے کے بعد کفن کے گرہ کھول دے۔ اس کی دلیل

[434] (33) Untie the knot. At the time of shrouding, if there was a risk of it opening, it was said to tie a knot. Now after laying the deceased in the grave, untie the knot of the shroud. Its proof is this athar: from Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i): 'When the deceased is entered into the grave, untie all the knots from him.' Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i). The commentary explains the rationale: when shrouding, it is permissible to tie the shroud to prevent it from opening before burial, but after the deceased is placed in the grave, those knots should be untied. The evidence is the athar from Ibrahim. This is a sunnah practice in the Hanafi school.

The Sunnah of Sealing the Lahd with Sun-Dried Bricks
Ruling with proof on sealing the lahd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sealing the lahd and identify the proof from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Sun-dried bricks on the lahd are sunnah, proven by the Prophet’s own burial.

The burial of a Muslim involves careful preparation of the grave. One such detail is how the niche (lahd) is sealed after placing the body. This lesson examines the ruling on using sun-dried bricks (labin) for this purpose, as established in the Hanafi school, and the evidence from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing sun-dried bricks on the lahd to close it. The Hanafi ruling is that this is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Sa‘d ibn Abi Waqqas requesting a lahd and labin like for the Prophet ﷺ, and the practice of ‘Ali ibn Husayn at the Prophet’s grave.
References: Muslim, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit request and the Companion’s action indicate that using sun-dried bricks is a recommended practice (sunnah). The imperative form (insabu) in the narration supports desirability.
The hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni dalala, hence sunnah not wajib.
4
Note the material restriction
The text specifies 'sun-dried bricks' (labin), not baked bricks or other materials. The Hanafi school considers baked bricks makruh because of fire involvement.
Baked bricks (ajur) are disliked; sun-dried bricks preserve the sunnah.
5
Understand the ruling's application
This ruling applies to the lahd (niche) burial. For shaqq (trench) burial, the ruling may differ. The sunnah is to use sun-dried bricks if available.
If labin are unavailable, any earth material may be used, but the sunnah is specific.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۵] (۳۴) اور لحد میں کچی اینٹ برابر کر کے ڈالی جائے۔ ا لحد کے دائیں کنارے میں میت کو رکھ دی جاتی ہے اس لئے لحد کے منہ پر کچی اینٹ برابر کر کے ڈالی جائے جس سے لحد کا منہ بند ہو جائے۔

اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان سعد بن ابی وقاص قال في مرضه الذي هلك فيه الحدوا لحدا وانصبوا على لبنا نصبا كما صنع برسول الله الا الله (ج) (مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل فی استحباب اللحد ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۹۶۶) عن علی ابن حسین انهم على قبر رسول الله الا الله نصبوا اللين نصبا ( و ) ( مصنف ابن ابى شبيبة ۱۲۹، في اللبن ينصب على القبر او بینی بناءج ثالث ص ۲۳، نمبر ۱۱۷۲۹) اس اثر سے اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لحد میں کچی اینٹ ڈالی جائے۔
[435] (34) And place sun-dried bricks evenly on the lahd. The deceased is placed in the right side of the lahd, so sun-dried bricks should be placed evenly at the opening of the lahd to close it.

Its proof is this hadith: Sa'd bin Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died, 'Make a lahd for me and place sun-dried bricks on me as was done for the Messenger of Allah.' (Muslim, chapter on recommendation of lahd) And from Ali bin Husain that they placed sun-dried bricks on the grave of the Messenger of Allah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this athar and hadith, it is known that sun-dried bricks should be placed in the lahd.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the manner of sealing the lahd (niche). The matn says to place sun-dried bricks (unbaked) evenly over the lahd. The commentary explains the purpose: to close the opening of the lahd after placing the body. The proof is the hadith of Sa'd bin Abi Waqqas, who requested treatment like the Prophet's burial, and the practice of Ali bin Husain at the Prophet's grave. This establishes the sunnah of using sun-dried bricks.

Key Terms
لحد (lahd): A niche dug on the side of the grave where the body is placed.
لبن (labin): Sun-dried bricks, not baked by fire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Using Baked Bricks, Wood, and Bamboo for the Grave
Ruling statement on disliked materials for grave covering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using baked bricks, wood, and bamboo for grave covering and explain the legal reasoning based on the grave's purpose.

Core Idea
The grave is meant to decay; durable materials contradict this purpose and are thus disliked.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri presents a straightforward ruling on three materials used for grave construction. What makes this ruling jurisprudentially rich is the explicit reasoning: the grave is intended for disintegration. The lesson unpacks the ruling and the underlying legal cause.

Guided Path
1
Extract the rulings
Identify the legal classification (hukm) for each material mentioned: baked bricks and wood are makruh; bamboo is ja'iz (permissible).
Makruh here is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Identify the illah (legal cause)
The passage states the reason: the grave is meant to decay and become desolate. Durable and fire-hardened materials prevent this.
The illah is the durability and fire-hardening of the material.
3
Apply the illah to hypothetical materials
Using the identified illah, consider other materials like concrete, metal, or simple earth. Durable materials are makruh; perishable ones are permissible.
This is a qiyas application of the stated illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۳۶] (۳۵) مکروہ ہے پکی اینٹ اور تختے، اور کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے بانس ڈالنے میں۔ اری قبر بوسیدہ ہونے اور ویران ہونے کے لئے ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر ایسی چیزیں بنانا جو دیر پا ہو اور آگ سے پکی ہو وہ مکروہ ہے۔ اس لئے یکی اینٹیں دینا مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں آگ کا اثر ہے اور دیر پا ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح مضبوط قسم کا تختہ دینا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ دیر پارہتا ہے۔ البتہ بانس چونکہ دیر پانہیں ہے اس لئے وہ جائز ہے۔
[436] (35) Baked bricks and wood are disliked, and there is no harm in placing bamboo. Because the grave is meant to decay and become desolate. Therefore, building on it such things that are durable and hardened by fire is disliked. Hence, placing baked bricks is disliked because it involves the effect of fire and is durable. Similarly, placing strong wood is disliked because it is enduring. However, bamboo, since it is not enduring, is permissible.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining the rationality behind the dislike. The matn declares baked bricks (آجر) and wood (خشب) as makruh (disliked), while bamboo (قصب) is permissible. The commentary provides the reasoning: the purpose of the grave is to allow the body to decay and return to the earth. Therefore, using materials that are permanent or fire-hardened contradicts this purpose. Baked bricks have been hardened by fire and are long-lasting, so they are disliked. Strong wood is also durable. Bamboo, being less durable, is allowed. This ruling is based on the principle that the grave should be simple and not impede natural decay.

Key Terms
آجر (ajur): Baked bricks, hardened by fire.
خشب (khashab): Wood, especially strong planks.
قصب (qasab): Bamboo or reeds, which are perishable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which material is considered permissible (ja'iz) for covering the grave according to this passage?
A) Baked bricks
B) Strong wood
C) Bamboo
D) Metal plates

Key Takeaway
Baked bricks and strong wood are disliked for grave covering due to durability; bamboo is permissible because it is perishable.

Funeral Rites for a Crying Newborn
Ruling on a child who cries after birth and dies shortly thereafter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a newborn who shows signs of life and dies, and distinguish it from a stillborn.

Core Idea
A newborn who cries or shows any sign of life is a full person in death; stillborns are not.

This lesson addresses a common situation: a newborn infant dies shortly after birth. Does it receive full burial rites? The Hanafi school bases the ruling on whether the infant showed any sign of life, such as crying. This lesson unpacks the criteria and the resulting obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text contrasts a child who cries (istahalla) with one who does not. Crying is a definitive sign of life, triggering full funeral rites.
2
Extract the general rule
The commentator states that any sign of life (crying, movement, breathing) activates funeral rites. Signs are not limited to crying.
3
List the rites for a live-born child
From the text: the child is named, given ghusl (bath), shrouded, and funeral prayer is performed.
4
Note the treatment for a stillborn
If no sign of life, no ghusl, no prayer; the body is simply wrapped in cloth and buried.
5
Reflect on the underlying principle
The ruling hinges on confirming life after birth. This ensures the child is treated with full dignity as a Muslim deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استهل. ولادت کے بعد جو رویا ہو تو اس کا نام رکھا جائے گا اور غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور اگر نہیں رویا تو ایک ٹکڑے میں لپیٹ دیا جائے گا اور دفن کر دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ زندہ پیدا ہوا ہو اور بعد میں مرا ہو تو اس پر میت کے سارے احکام جاری ہوں گے۔ اور اگر مردہ پیدا ہوا ہو تو وہ گوشت کے لوتھڑے کی طرح ہے اس پر میت کے احکام جاری نہیں ہونگے رونا زندگی کی علامت ہے، اسی طرح کوئی اور علامت سے زندگی کا پتہ چل جائے تو اس پر میت کے احکام جاری ہو نگے ورنہ نہیں۔ اگر زندگی کا پتہ چلا تو اس بچے کا نام رکھا جائے گا۔ اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز
And whoever cries [at birth]. A child who cries after birth: his name will be given, he will be given a bath, and funeral prayer will be performed over him. And if he did not cry, he will be wrapped in a piece of cloth and buried, and no funeral prayer will be performed over him. The basic rule is: if he was born alive and then died, all rulings of the deceased apply to him. And if he was born dead, he is like a piece of flesh; the rulings of the deceased do not apply to him. Crying is a sign of life; similarly, if life is detected by any other sign, then the rulings of the deceased apply, otherwise not. If life is detected, the child is given a name, given a bath, and prayer is performed over him.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The matn 'ومن استهل' means 'and whoever cries [at birth]'. The commentator explains that a newborn who cries after birth (indicating life) and then dies is treated as a full deceased Muslim: naming, washing, shrouding, and funeral prayer are obligatory. If the child is stillborn (no cry or other sign of life), it is not given a bath or prayer; it is merely wrapped in a cloth and buried. The commentator derives a general rule: any sign of life (like crying, moving, sucking) activates all funeral rites. This is the Hanafi position: a child born alive but dying soon after receives full funeral rites.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): to cry at birth, indicating the child was born alive

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child is wrapped in a cloth and buried without prayer.
B) The child is given a name, given a bath, and funeral prayer is performed.
C) The child is given a bath but no prayer.
D) The child is not named but given a bath and prayer.

Key Takeaway
A newborn who shows any sign of life is entitled to full funeral rites; a stillborn is not.

Funeral Prayer for a Child: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on prayer over child with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer for a child, identify the sign of life that triggers the obligation, and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer for a child is fard kifayah only if the child showed signs of life at birth (istihlal, such as crying).

In this passage from a classical Hanafi fiqh text, the author addresses a common scenario: the death of a newborn. The ruling distinguishes between a child born alive (tifl) and a stillborn (suqt). The key proof comes from two hadiths where the Prophet explicitly commands prayer over a child, but with the condition that the child showed life. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly performing funeral rites in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of deceased children
The passage mentions two cases: a child who is born alive (istahalla, i.e., cried or showed signs of life) and a stillborn (who did not cry, lam yastahill).
The Arabic verb 'istahalla' specifically refers to the child crying out.
2
State the ruling for each category
For the live-born child: he is named, given ghusl, and funeral prayer is offered. For the stillborn: he is wrapped in a cloth and buried without prayer.
The funeral prayer for a live-born child is fard kifayah (communal obligation).
3
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah where the Prophet said: 'The rider goes behind the funeral procession, the pedestrian walks wherever he wishes, and the child is prayed over.'
This is a direct command indicating obligation.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (indication) of the hadith
The phrase 'wal-tiflu yusalla 'alayh' (and the child is prayed over) is a general command. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub).
The word 'tifl' here refers to a living child, as clarified by the second hadith.
5
Confirm with the second hadith (Jabir) and note the condition
The hadith of Jabir adds a condition: 'when the child cries (istahalla), prayer is offered over him and he inherits.' This specifies that only children who cry (show life) receive the prayer.
The two hadiths together establish the ruling: prayer is for live-born children only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
بعد الولادة سمی و غسل و صلی علیه وان لم يستهل ادرج في خرقة ودفن ولم يصل عليه.
بھی پڑھی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن المغيرة بن شعبة انه ذكر ان رسول الله قال الراكب خلف الجنازة والماشي حيث شاء منها والطفل يصلى عليه (الف) ( نسائی شریف، باب الصلوة علی الاطفال ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۹۵۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کا انتقال ہو جائے تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی ۔ اور طفل اسی وقت کہتے ہیں جب کہ اس میں زندگی ہو ورنہ تو وہ گوشت کا لوتھڑا ہے۔ عن عن جابر بن عبد الله قال قال رسول الله الا الله اذا استهل الصبي صلى عليه وورث (ب) ( ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء فی صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلوة على الطفل ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۱۵۰۸/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلوۃ علی الصغير والسقط و میراث ص ۵۳۰ نمبر ۶۵۹۵ للبيهقي ، باب السقط يغسل ویکفن و یصلی علیه ان استقل او عرفت له الحياة ج رابع ص ۱۳، نمبر ۶۷۸۳) اس اثر سے اوپر کے مسئلے کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا سوار جنازہ کے پیچھے رہے اور پیدل چلنے والا جدھر چاہے چلے، اور بچے پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی (ب) رسول اللہ نے فرمایا جب بچہ
روئے تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے اور وہ وارث ہوگا۔
Book of Prayer. After birth, he is named, washed, and prayer is offered over him. And if he did not cry out, he is wrapped in a cloth and buried, and no prayer is offered over him. It will be read (prayer). The evidence is this hadith from al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that he mentioned that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The rider goes behind the funeral procession, and the pedestrian goes wherever he wishes from it, and the child is prayed over.' From this hadith it is understood that when a child passes away, prayer is offered over him. And the term 'child' applies only when there is life in him; otherwise, he is a piece of flesh. From Jabir ibn Abdullah that he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, when a child cries out, prayer is offered over him and he inherits.' This narration supports the above ruling. Footnote (a): He said: 'The rider remains behind the funeral, and the pedestrian goes wherever he wishes, and the child is prayed over.' (b): The Messenger of Allah said: 'When a child cries, prayer is offered over him and he will be an heir.'
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Prayer. The author states the legal rule: a child born alive is named, given funeral washing, and the funeral prayer is offered. If the child does not cry (i.e., is stillborn), it is simply wrapped in cloth and buried without prayer. The term 'child' (tifl) refers to one who shows signs of life at birth. The author then provides two hadith proofs: first, the hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah where the Prophet explicitly states that the child is prayed over, establishing the obligation (wujub) of the funeral prayer for children who die after live birth. Second, the hadith of Jabir adds that if the child cries (istahalla), he is prayed over and also inherits, confirming the ruling. The footnote clarifies that 'crying' is the sign of life. In the Hanafi school, the funeral prayer for a child who dies after live birth is fard kifayah, just as for an adult. A stillborn is not given funeral prayer because there was no life.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): The child cried out or made any sound indicating life at birth
طفل (tifl): A child born alive with signs of life
سقط (suqt): A stillborn child (one that did not cry at birth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the parents request it

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer for a child is only offered if the child showed signs of life at birth (istihlal); otherwise, it is buried without prayer.

Definition and Rulings of the Complete Martyr
Definition and funeral rulings for a complete martyr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of a complete martyr and apply the ruling that such a martyr is not washed, is enshrouded in his own clothes, and is prayed over.

Core Idea
A complete martyr is not washed; his clothes serve as shroud, and the funeral prayer is performed.

The martyr holds a special station in Islam, but not all who die in battle are treated identically in funeral rites. The Hanafi school distinguishes a 'complete martyr' (shahid kamil) who meets specific conditions and whose body is not washed. This lesson examines the three categories of complete martyr and the rulings derived from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at the Battle of Uhud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions for a complete martyr
The text lists three scenarios: killed by polytheists, found dead on battlefield with wound marks, or killed unjustly by a Muslim without diyah obligation. Determine the common element: no worldly benefit after wounding and no compensation.
The third scenario requires that no diyah is due; otherwise qisas is due.
2
Distinguish complete martyr from other martyrs
A complete martyr is not washed. Other martyrs (e.g., one who receives worldly benefit after being wounded, or one for whom diyah is paid) are washed normally.
The key is whether the martyr was 'completely wronged' (mazlum kamil).
3
State the funeral rulings
The complete martyr is not given ghusl, is enshrouded in his own clothes (with adjustments as needed), and the funeral prayer is offered over him. These are fard kifayah.
If clothes are insufficient, additional cloth is added; if excessive, surplus is removed.
4
Examine the dalil from the Sunnah
The Prophet ﷺ ordered the martyrs of Uhud to be buried in their blood without washing, and commanded removal of iron and leather but not their clothes. This is found in authentic ahadith.
Thubut is zanni (ahad) but dalala is qati (explicit prohibition of ghusl).
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that martyrs are also washed, relying on general hadiths about washing the deceased. The Hanafi school maintains the specificity of the Uhud incident.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهيد
[ ٤٣٩] (١) الشهيد من قتله المشركون او وجد في المعركة وبه اثر الجراحة او قتله المسلمون ظلما ولم يجب بقتله دية [۴۴۰](۲) فيكفن و يصلى عليه ولا يغسل
باب الشهيد )
ضروری نوٹ اس شہید کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا جو شہدائے احد کی طرح ہو۔ یعنی کافروں نے ظلما قتل کیا ہو اور زخم لگنے کے بعد دنیا سے کوئی فائدہ نہ اٹھایا ہو اور انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔ اور اس کے قتل کی وجہ سے دیت، قصاص یا کوئی معاوضہ بھی نہ لیا جا سکا ہوتا کہ مکمل مظلوم ہوکر مرے۔ ایسا شہید کامل شہید ہے۔ اس کے یہ احکام ہیں جو آگے آرہے ہیں۔ [۴۳۹) (۱) شہید ( کامل ) وہ ہے (۱) جس کو مشرکین نے قتل کیا ہو (۲) یا میدان جنگ میں پایا گیا ہو اور اس پر زخم کا اثر ہو (۳) یا مسلمان نے ظلما قتل کیا ہو اور اس کے قتل کی وجہ سے کوئی دیت لازم نہ ہوئی ہو۔
یہاں شہید کی تین تعریفیں ہیں یا تین قسمیں ہیں جو کامل شہید شمار کئے جاتے ہیں۔ پہلا یہ ہے کہ مشرک نے اس کو قتل کیا ہو۔ دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ مشرک نے مکمل قتل تو نہ کیا ہو لیکن میدان جنگ میں زخمی پایا گیا ہو پھر دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھائے بغیر انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔ میدان جنگ میں پایا جانا دلیل ہے کہ اس کو کفار نے قتل کیا ہے۔ تیسری مشکل یہ ہے کہ قتل تو مسلمان نے ہی کیا ہے لیکن قتل اس انداز سے کیا ہے کہ اس کی وجہ سے دیت اور مال لازم نہیں آتا ہے بلکہ قصاص لازم آتا ہے۔ اگر دیت اور مال لازم آتا تو دیت لینے کی وجہ سے ظلم میں کمی واقع ہوگئی اس لئے مکمل مظلوم نہیں رہا اور نہ کمل شہید ہوا اس لئے اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر دیت لازم نہیں ہوئی ہو تو مال نہ لینے کی وجہ سے مکمل مظلوم ہوا۔ اس لئے اب وہ شہدائے احد کے درجہ میں ہوا اس لئے اس کو غسل نہیں جائیگا۔
(۴۴۰ (۲) پس کفن دیا جائے گا اور نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ کفن دیا جائے گا اور نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جابر قال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ادفنوهم في دمائهم يعني يوم احد ولم يغسلهم (الف) بخاری شریف، باب من لم ير غسل الشہید ص ۷۹ انمبر ۱۳۴۶ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب في الشهيد يغسل ج ثانی ص ۹۱ نمبر ۳۱۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے کپڑے کے ساتھ کفن دیکر دفن کیا جائے۔ اور جو زیادہ ہو اس کو نکال لیا جائے۔ اور جو کم ہو اس کا اضافہ کیا جائے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال امر رسول الله الله بقتلى احد ان ينزع عنهم الحديد والجلود وان يدفنوا بدمائهم و ثيابهم (ب) (ابود او د شریف ، باب فی الشہید يغسل ج ثانی ص 91 نمبر ۳۱۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفن کے لائق جو کپڑے یا چیزیں نہ ہوں ان کو نکال دیے جائیں اور جو کپڑے کفن کے لائق ہوں وہ ان
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا شہیدوں کو اس کے خون میں دفن کر و یعنی جنگ احد کے دن اور ان کو نسل نہیں دیا ( ب ) آپ نے احد کے مقتولین کے بارے میں حکم دیا کہ ان سے لوہے کا سامان اور چمڑے کا سامان نکال دو، اور ان کے خون اور ان کے کپڑوں میں دفن کرو۔
Chapter of the Martyr.
[439] (1) The martyr is one whom the polytheists killed, or one found on the battlefield with the effect of a wound, or one killed unjustly by Muslims and no blood money (diyah) was obligatory for his killing. [440] (2) So he is enshrouded, prayed over, and not washed.
Essential note: That martyr will not be given ghusl (washed) who is like the martyrs of Uhud, i.e., the polytheists killed him unjustly and he did not benefit from the world after being wounded, and then died; and no diyah, qisas, or any compensation could be taken for his killing, so he died completely wronged. Such a martyr is a complete (kamil) martyr. These are his rulings that will come. [439] (1) The complete martyr is one: (1) whom polytheists killed, (2) or found on the battlefield with the effect of a wound, (3) or a Muslim killed him unjustly and no diyah became obligatory for his killing. Here are three definitions or three types that are considered complete martyrs. The first is that a polytheist killed him. The second is that a polytheist did not completely kill him but he was found wounded on the battlefield, then he died without benefiting from the world. Being found on the battlefield is evidence that the disbelievers killed him. The third is that a Muslim killed him but in such a way that no diyah or wealth became obligatory, rather qisas became obligatory. If diyah or wealth had become obligatory, then due to taking the diyah, the oppression would be lessened, so he would not be completely wronged and not a complete martyr; thus he would be given ghusl. But if diyah did not become obligatory, then due to not taking wealth, he is completely wronged. Therefore, he is now at the level of the martyrs of Uhud, so he will not be given ghusl.
(440) (2) So he is enshrouded, prayed over, and not given ghusl. He is enshrouded and not given ghusl. The evidence is the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet said: 'Bury them in their blood,' meaning on the day of Uhud, 'and do not wash them.' (Footnote a) From this hadith it is understood that the martyr is not given ghusl. He is buried with his clothes as his shroud. If there is excess, it is removed; if there is deficiency, it is supplemented. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded regarding the slain of Uhud to remove from them iron and hides, and to bury them with their blood and their clothes.' (Footnote b) From this hadith it is understood that whatever clothes or items are suitable for the shroud, they are left, and what is not suitable is removed.
Footnote (a): The Prophet said: 'Bury the martyrs in their blood,' meaning the day of Uhud, 'and do not wash them.' (b): The Prophet commanded the slain of Uhud to remove iron and hides from them, and to bury them with their blood and clothes.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Chapter of the Martyr. It defines three categories of complete martyr (shahid kamil): (1) killed by polytheists; (2) found dead on battlefield with wound marks; (3) killed unjustly by a Muslim such that no diyah is obligatory (i.e., the killer must undergo qisas). The common factor is that the martyr did not benefit from worldly goods after being wounded and no compensation was received. The ruling for such a martyr: he is not washed (ghusl), but is enshrouded (takfeen) in his own clothes, and the funeral prayer is offered over him. The author cites two ahadith: the first from Jabir (Bukhari no. 1346, Abu Dawud no. 3135) that the Prophet ordered the martyrs of Uhud to be buried in their blood without washing. The second from Ibn 'Abbas (Abu Dawud no. 3134) that the Prophet ordered removal of iron and leather (armor) but to bury them with their clothes. This shows that the martyr's clothing serves as his shroud; if it is insufficient, additional cloth is added; if excessive, the surplus is removed. The Hanafi school follows this ruling: the complete martyr is not washed, but is enshrouded and prayed over.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahid): A complete martyr (shahid kamil) as defined by three categories
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the deceased
كفن (kafan): Shroud; for the martyr, his own clothes serve as shroud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three categories of complete martyr according to the Hanafi text?
A) Killed by polytheists
B) Found on battlefield with wound marks
C) Killed unjustly by a Muslim and diyah becomes obligatory
D) Killed unjustly by a Muslim with no diyah obligatory

Key Takeaway
The complete martyr is defined by specific conditions, and his funeral rites exclude washing while including prayer and burial in his own clothes.
