Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Definition and Rulings for the Complete Martyr
Defines the complete martyr and states burial rulings with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the complete martyr (shahid kamil) according to the Hanafi school, list the three categories, and identify the rulings on ghusl, kafan, and salat al-janazah with their proofs.

Core Idea
A complete martyr is not washed but is shrouded and prayed over — his blood bears witness, not his body.

The term 'martyr' (shahid) carries specific legal weight in Hanafi fiqh. Not every slain Muslim is treated the same in burial rites. This lesson defines the complete martyr (shahid kamil) — the one who dies under complete oppression without worldly benefit or compensation. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying the rulings of ghusl, kafan, and salat al-janazah, and for navigating the well-known inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school over funeral prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the complete martyr. State the three rulings: no ghusl, must be shrouded, funeral prayer must be performed.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith proofs cited: (1) Hadith of Jabir – 'Bury them in their blood' for no ghusl; (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas – remove iron/leather but keep clothes for shrouding; (3) Hadith of Ibn Abbas and Uqba – Prophet prayed over martyrs for salat.
Each ruling has its own dalil.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling. For ghusl: the Prophet did not wash them, so washing is omitted. For kafan: clothes are kept as shroud. For salat: the Prophet performed prayer, so it is legislated.
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is evidence of obligation or permissibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the Shafi'i objection: they hold that no funeral prayer is offered for the martyr, citing a different narration of Jabir where the Prophet did not pray.
The dispute is over the interpretation of conflicting hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred: multiple authentic hadith show the Prophet praying over martyrs, and prayer is for forgiveness and elevation of ranks, which is beneficial for the martyr.
The Hanafi school gives weight to the practice of the Prophet and the general principle of prayer for the deceased.

باب الشهيد

ضروری نوٹ: اس شہید کو غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا جو شہدائے احد کی طرح ہو۔ یعنی کافروں نے ظلماً قتل کیا ہو اور زخم لگنے کے بعد دنیا سے کوئی فائدہ نہ اٹھایا ہو اور انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔ اور اس کے قتل کی وجہ سے دیت، قصاص یا کوئی معاوضہ بھی نہ لیا جا سکا ہوتا کہ مکمل مظلوم ہوکر مرے۔ ایسا شہید کامل شہید ہے۔ اس کے یہ احکام ہیں جو آگے آرہے ہیں۔

[۴۳۹] (۱) شہید (کامل) وہ ہے (۱) جس کو مشرکین نے قتل کیا ہو (۲) یا میدان جنگ میں پایا گیا ہو اور اس پر زخم کا اثر ہو (۳) یا مسلمان نے ظلماً قتل کیا ہو اور اس کے قتل کی وجہ سے کوئی دیت لازم نہ ہوئی ہو۔

یہاں شہید کی تین تعریفیں ہیں یا تین قسمیں ہیں جو کامل شہید شمار کئے جاتے ہیں۔ پہلا یہ ہے کہ مشرک نے اس کو قتل کیا ہو۔ دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ مشرک نے مکمل قتل تو نہ کیا ہو لیکن میدان جنگ میں زخمی پایا گیا ہو پھر دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھائے بغیر انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔ میدان جنگ میں پایا جانا دلیل ہے کہ اس کو کفار نے قتل کیا ہے۔ تیسری مشکل یہ ہے کہ قتل تو مسلمان نے ہی کیا ہے لیکن قتل اس انداز سے کیا ہے کہ اس کی وجہ سے دیت اور مال لازم نہیں آتا ہے بلکہ قصاص لازم آتا ہے۔ اگر دیت اور مال لازم آتا تو دیت لینے کی وجہ سے ظلم میں کمی واقع ہوگئی اس لئے مکمل مظلوم نہیں رہا اور نہ کامل شہید ہوا اس لئے اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر دیت لازم نہیں ہوئی ہو تو مال نہ لینے کی وجہ سے مکمل مظلوم ہوا۔ اس لئے اب وہ شہدائے احد کے درجہ میں ہوا اس لئے اس کو غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔

[۴۴۰] (۲) پس کفن دیا جائے گا اور نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ کفن دیا جائے گا غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن جابر قال: قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "ادفنوهم في دمائهم" يعني يوم أحد ولم يغسلهم. (بخاری شریف، باب من لم ير غسل الشہید ص ۷۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۶ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب في الشهيد يغسل ج ثانی ص ۹۱ نمبر ۳۱۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید کو غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے کپڑے کے ساتھ کفن دیکر دفن کیا جائے۔ اور جو زیادہ ہو اس کو نکال لیا جائے۔ اور جو کم ہو اس کا اضافہ کیا جائے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن ابن عباس قال: أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقتلى أحد أن ينزع عنهم الحديد والجلود وأن يدفنوا بدمائهم وثيابهم. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الشہید يغسل ج ثانی ص 91 نمبر ۳۱۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفن کے لائق جو کپڑے یا چیزیں نہ ہوں ان کو نکال دیے جائیں اور جو کپڑے کفن کے لائق ہوں وہ ان کے ساتھ ہی رکھے جائیں۔ اور کفن میں جو کمی رہ جائے اس کو پوری کی جائے۔

شہید پر نماز پڑھی جائے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن ابن عباس قال: أتى بهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم أحد فجعل يصلي على عشرة عشرة وحمزة هو كما هو يرفعون وهو كما هو موضوع. (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوة على الشهداء ج ۲ ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۵۱۵ / سنن البیهقی، باب من زعم ان النبی صلی الله علیہ وسلم علی شهداء أحد ج رابع ص ۱۸ نمبر ۶۸۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شهداء احد پر آپ نے نماز پڑھی۔ (۲) نماز ترقی درجات کے لئے اور استغفار کے لئے ہے۔ اور یہ بچوں اور نبی کے لئے بھی جائز ہے۔ اس لئے شہید کے لئے بھی کیا جائے۔ (۳) خود بخاری میں اس حدیث میں موجود ہے: عن عقبة بن عامر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج يوماً فصلى على أهل أحد صلاته على الميت ثم انصرف إلى المنبر. (بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی الشہید ص ۱۷۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید پر نماز پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلوة على الشهيد وغسله ج ثالث ص ۵۴۲ نمبر ۶۶۳۷/۶۶۳۶ میں شہید پر نماز پڑھنے کے بارے میں تفصیل موجود ہے. فليراجع!

قائد: امام شافعی کے نزدیک شہید پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن جابر بن عبد الله ... وأمر بدفنهم في دمائهم ولم يغسل ولم يصل عليهم. (بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة على الشہید ص ۱۷۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۳ / ابوداؤد شریف باب فی الشید يغسل ج ثانی ص ۹۱ نمبر ۳۱۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔

ہمارا عمل پہلی احادیث پر ہے۔
Chapter of the Martyr

Necessary Note: This martyr will not be given ghusl who is like the martyrs of Uhud. That is, the disbelievers unjustly killed him, and after being wounded he did not derive any worldly benefit, and he passed away. And due to his killing, blood-money (diyah), retaliation (qisas), or any compensation could not be taken, so he died completely oppressed. Such a martyr is a complete martyr (shahid kamil). These are his rulings that follow.

[439] (1) The (complete) martyr is: (1) one whom the polytheists killed, or (2) one found on the battlefield with the effect of a wound, or (3) one whom a Muslim killed unjustly and for whose killing no blood-money (diyah) is obligatory.

Here are three definitions or three categories counted as complete martyrs. First: a polytheist killed him. Second: a polytheist did not completely kill him but he was found wounded on the battlefield and then passed away without benefiting from the world. Being found on the battlefield is evidence that the disbelievers killed him. Third: a Muslim killed him but in a manner that does not obligate blood-money or wealth but rather retaliation. If blood-money or wealth were obligated, then due to taking blood-money the oppression would be reduced, so he would not be completely oppressed and not a complete martyr; therefore he would be given ghusl. But if blood-money is not obligatory, then due to not taking wealth, he is completely oppressed. Thus he becomes of the rank of the martyrs of Uhud, so he will not be given ghusl.

[440] (2) So he is given a shroud (kafan) and prayer (salat) is performed over him, and he is not given ghusl. He is given a shroud, not given ghusl; the proof is this hadith: from Jabir who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Bury them in their blood" meaning on the day of Uhud, and he did not wash them. (Bukhari, Bab man lam yara ghusl al-shahid, p. 79, no. 1346; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-shahid yughsal, vol. 2, p. 91, no. 3135) From this hadith it is known that the martyr is not given ghusl. He is buried with his clothes as a shroud. What is extra is removed, and what is insufficient is supplemented. The proof is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah ordered concerning the slain of Uhud that the iron and leather be removed from them and that they be buried in their blood and their clothes. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-shahid yughsal, vol. 2, p. 91, no. 3134) From this hadith it is known that clothes or items not suitable for the shroud are removed, and those suitable remain with them. Any deficiency in the shroud is made up.

Prayer is performed over the martyr; the proof is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought the martyrs of Uhud, and he began to pray over them ten by ten, while Hamza remained in his place, and they were lifted while he remained in his place. (Ibn Majah, Bab ma ja'a fi al-salat 'ala al-shuhada', vol. 2, p. 216, no. 1515; Bayhaqi, Bab man za'ama anna al-nabi salla 'ala shuhada' Uhud, vol. 4, p. 18, no. 6804) From this hadith it is known that he prayed over the martyrs of Uhud. (2) Prayer is for elevation of ranks and for seeking forgiveness, and it is permissible for children and prophets, so it is also done for the martyr. (3) In Bukhari itself this hadith is present: from Uqba ibn Amir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out one day and prayed over the people of Uhud as his prayer over the deceased, then returned to the pulpit. (Bukhari, Bab al-salat 'ala al-shahid, p. 179, no. 1344) From this hadith it is known that prayer can be performed over the martyr. In Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-salat 'ala al-shahid wa ghuslihi, vol. 3, p. 542, nos. 6637/6636, details about praying over the martyr are present. So refer to it!

Qa'id: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the funeral prayer will not be performed over the martyr. Their proof is this hadith: from Jabir ibn Abd Allah ... and he ordered them to be buried in their blood, and he did not wash nor pray over them. (Bukhari, Bab al-salat 'ala al-shahid, p. 179, no. 1343; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-shahid yughsal, vol. 2, p. 91, no. 3135) From this hadith it is known that the funeral prayer is not performed over the martyr.

Our practice is upon the first hadiths.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri defines the complete martyr (shahid kamil) and lists his rulings. The author first states three categories of complete martyr: killed by polytheists, found on the battlefield with wounds, or killed unjustly by a Muslim without liability for blood-money. The commentary explains that the key is that the martyr did not derive any worldly benefit after being wounded and no compensation was taken, making him completely oppressed like the martyrs of Uhud. The ruling for such a martyr is that he is given a shroud (kafan), the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is performed, but he is not washed (ghusl). The author provides multiple hadith proofs: the Prophet's command to bury the martyrs of Uhud in their blood without washing, the instruction to remove iron and leather but retain clothes for shrouding, and the practice of the Prophet praying over them ten by ten. The passage then addresses the Shafi'i view that no funeral prayer is offered, citing a different hadith. The Hanafi response is that the prayer is performed based on the stronger evidence of the Prophet's action, as prayer is for forgiveness and elevation of ranks.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahīd): A Muslim killed unjustly in a state of complete oppression, without benefiting from worldly means after injury, and without compensation for his killing.
غسل (ghusl): The ritual washing of the deceased body; omitted for the complete martyr.
كفن (kafan): The shroud in which the deceased is buried. For the complete martyr, his clothing serves as the shroud, with any unsuitable items removed and deficiencies supplemented.
صلاة الجنازة (salāt al-janāzah): The funeral prayer performed over the deceased Muslim. For the complete martyr, it is performed according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the proof that the complete martyr is not given ghusl?
A) The hadith: 'Bury them in their blood' and the Prophet did not wash them.
B) The hadith: 'Remove the iron and leather from them.'
C) The hadith: 'He prayed over them ten by ten.'
D) The hadith: 'He went out and prayed over them as over the deceased.'

Key Takeaway
The complete martyr is defined by complete oppression without worldly benefit or compensation; he is not washed but is shrouded in his clothes and the funeral prayer is performed over him.

The Ghusl of a Junub Martyr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl for a martyred junub or minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding ghusl for a junub or minor martyr, identify the proof each side relies on, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
A junub martyr's ghusl is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa relies on angels washing Hanzalah; the Sahibayn uphold the general rule of no ghusl for martyrs.

This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi conflict: does the general rule of not washing martyrs apply even when the martyr was in a state of janabah? Abu Hanifa rules that ghusl is still wajib, citing the hadith of Hanzalah (radi Allahu 'anhu) who was washed by angels. The Sahibayn argue against it, maintaining the general exception. Understanding the proof structure is crucial for recognizing how specific evidence (dalil khas) can qualify a general principle (amr amm).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing positions
Read the first sentence: 'And if a junub becomes a martyr, he is given ghusl according to Abu Hanifa... and likewise the minor. And the two Sahibayn said: Both are not given ghusl.' Note the clear statement of the dispute.
The word 'صبي' (minor) is also included; the same ruling applies.
2
Isolate Abu Hanifa's proof
The text then provides the reasoning for Abu Hanifa: the hadith of Hanzalah, who was junub when he was martyred at Uhud, and the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) said the angels washed him. This indicates that janabah necessitates ghusl even for a martyr.
The hadith is cited from Sunan al-Bayhaqi. Identify the key phrase: 'ألا لذلك غسلته الملائكة' (Ah, for that reason the angels washed him).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
Although not detailed in the text, the Sahibayn rely on the general principle that martyrs are not washed (based on other authentic hadith). They view the Hanzalah incident as a special miracle specific to him (khass), not a general rule.
This is a classic case of takhsis (specification) of a general ruling by a specific incident.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a junub martyr is found, Abu Hanifa's followers would perform ghusl; followers of the Sahibayn would not. This has practical implications for funeral arrangements.
The mufta bihi in the later Hanafi school is the Sahibayn's view, but both positions are transmitted.
5
Note the later tarjih
Many later Hanafi jurists (e.g., in Al-Hidayah) prefer the Sahibayn's view as the operative ruling for fatwa. The student should be aware that the text presents Abu Hanifa's evidence but the school's practice may differ.
Tarjih (preference) is often based on the strength of the general evidence and the principle that the specific incident of Hanzalah is not generalizable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۴۱] (۳) واذا استشهد الجنب غسل عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وكذلك الصبى وقال صاحبيه لا يغسلان.

امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس لئے غسل دیا جائے گا کہ اگر چہ وہ شہید ہے لیکن غسل جنابت واجب ہے اس لئے غسل جنابت دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حضرت حنظلہ کو فرشتوں نے غسل دیا تھا۔ ان کی بیوی نے بتایا کہ وہ جنبی تھے۔ حدیث میں ہے: حدثنی یحیی بن عباد بن عبدالله ... حنظلة بن ابي عامر قال: فقال رسول الله: إن صاحبكم تغسله الملائكة فاسألوا صاحبته فقالت: خرج وهو جنب لما سمع الهائعة فقال رسول الله: ألا لذلك غسلته الملائكة. (سنن البیهقی، باب الجنب يستشهد في المعركة ج رابع ص ۲۲ نمبر ۶۸۱۴، کتاب الجنائز) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت حنظلہ جنبی تھے اور فرشتوں نے ان کو غسل دیا۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک اس لئے ان کو فرشتے غسل دے رہے ہیں۔
[441] (3) And if a junub becomes a martyr, he is given ghusl according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and likewise the minor. And the two Sahibayn said: Both are not given ghusl.

According to Imam Abu Hanifa, ghusl will be given because even though he is a martyr, the ghusl of janabah is obligatory, so ghusl of janabah will be given. Because the angels gave ghusl to Hadrat Hanzalah. His wife stated that he was junub. In the hadith: Yahya ibn Abbad ibn Abdullah narrated ... Hanzalah ibn Abi Amir said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, your companion is being washed by the angels, so ask his wife.' She said: 'He went out while he was junub when he heard the battle cry.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Ah, for that reason the angels washed him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-junub yastashhad fi al-ma'rakah, vol. 4, p. 22, no. 6814, Kitab al-Jana'iz) From this hadith it is known that Hadrat Hanzalah was junub and the angels washed him. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, for that reason the angels are washing him.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of ghusl to a martyr who was in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) at the time of martyrdom, and similarly for a minor (sabi) who dies as a martyr. The text reports the positions: Abu Hanifa rules that such a martyr must be given ghusl because the obligation of ghusl from janabah is not waived by martyrdom. He supports this with the well-known incident of Hanzalah (radi Allahu 'anhu), who was martyred at Uhud while junub and was washed by angels, as confirmed by the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no ghusl is given, as the general rule for martyrs (no ghusl) applies even to those in janabah, and the case of Hanzalah is a specific miracle not generalizable. The commentary emphasizes Abu Hanifa's evidence but notes the existence of the opposing view. In the later Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is often the Sahibayn's view, though both positions have authority.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl due to sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
صبي (ṣabī): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
شهيد (shahīd): A martyr who dies in battle fighting for the cause of Allah. In Hanafi fiqh, martyrs are given special funeral rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence for Abu Hanifa's view on washing a junub martyr?
A) The verse of purification (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6)
B) The practice of the Companions
C) The hadith that angels washed Hanzalah
D) The consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that a junub or minor martyr is not given ghusl, though Abu Hanifa himself ruled otherwise based on the hadith of Hanzalah.

Funeral Prayer for Martyrs: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on performing funeral prayer over martyrs with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on funeral prayer for martyrs, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi reliance on ahadith showing the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that funeral prayer is performed over martyrs, based on explicit Prophetic practice.

This passage presents a classical inter-madhhab dispute on whether the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is offered for martyrs. The Hanafi school affirms it, citing several ahadith where the Prophet prayed over the martyrs of Uhud. The Shafi'i school disagrees, relying on a hadith that the Prophet ordered their burial without prayer. Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school prioritizes different evidences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the Hanafi school performs the funeral prayer over martyrs. Note the key ahadith cited: Ibn Abbas (prayed ten by ten), Uqbah ibn Amir (prayed like regular funeral), and the reasoning that prayer seeks forgiveness and elevation, which applies to martyrs.
The passage explicitly says 'our practice is based on the first ahadith.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the funeral prayer is not performed for martyrs. Note the opposing evidence: the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet ordered burial without washing or prayer.
This hadith is recorded in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proof: the hadith of Jabir is a direct report of the Prophet's action. Understand why this might be considered strong evidence.
The Shafi'i school likely considers this a specific ruling for martyrs.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school acts on the ahadith that show the Prophet actually performing the prayer, considering them more specific or more authentic. They prioritize explicit actions over an apparent omission.
Multiple ahadith (Ibn Abbas, Uqbah) outweigh a single hadith in the Hanafi view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in a Hanafi community, the funeral prayer is offered for a martyr; in a Shafi'i community, it is not. This affects how a follower acts when a martyr dies.
This is a tangible difference in funeral rites.

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) for martyrs. The Hanafi position, which is the relied-upon view, is that the funeral prayer is performed over martyrs. The author cites multiple ahadith in support: the hadith of Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet praying over the martyrs of Uhud in groups, and the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir confirming that the Prophet prayed over them like a regular funeral prayer. The Hanafis argue that the purpose of the funeral prayer—seeking elevation and forgiveness—applies to martyrs as well. The Shafi'i school, by contrast, holds that the funeral prayer is not performed for martyrs, relying on the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet ordered them to be buried without washing or prayer. The author concludes that the Hanafi school acts upon the first set of ahadith, indicating that they consider those to be more authentic or more specific. The footnotes provide translations/paraphrases of the hadith references.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahid): A person killed in battle for the cause of Allah, who has specific rulings in funeral rites.
صلوة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer performed over the deceased Muslim.

The Intra-Hanafi Ruling on Washing a Martyr Who Was Junub
Intra-Hanafi dispute on washing a junub martyr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding washing a martyr who was junub, identify their respective proofs, and explain the practical consequence of this disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa washes the junub martyr; the Sahibayn do not—the obligation of ghusl clashes with the martyr's exemption.

This passage addresses a subtle disagreement within the Hanafi school: if a person dies as a martyr while in a state of major impurity (janabah), should they be washed? The general rule forbids washing martyrs, but janabah requires ghusl. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ on which rule prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the specific case (junub martyr and child martyr) and the disagreeing parties (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn).
The child martyr is included by analogy.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa rules that the junub martyr must be washed. His proof is the hadith of Hanzalah, whom angels washed despite his martyrdom.
This is a specific dalil that overrides the general rule.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn rule that the junub martyr is not washed. They rely on general ahadith forbidding washing of martyrs and draw an analogy with child martyrs based on sinlessness.
Their proof is the general principle and qiyas.
4
Analyse the response
Each side addresses the other's evidence: Abu Hanifa's supporters say the specific incident of Hanzalah is an exception; the Sahibayn may consider it abrogated or not generalizable.
This is a classic usul conflict between 'amm and khass.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a junub martyr is brought, one view washes, the other does not. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
Later Hanafi works often adopt the Sahibayn's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۴۱] (۳) واذا استشهد الجنب غسل عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وكذلك الصبى وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يغسلان [ ۴۴٢] ((۴) ولا يغسل عن الشهيد دمه ولا ينزع عنه ثيابه وينزع عنه الفرو والحشو والخف والسلاح [۴۴۳](۵) ومن ارتث غسل نزد یک جنبی شہید کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی وہ تمام احادیث ہے جن میں ہے کہ شہیدوں کو غسل نہ دیا جائے۔ بچے چونکہ گناہوں سے معصوم ہیں جس طرح شہید معصوم ہونگے، اس لئے شہید کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسی پر قیاس کر کے بچے کو بھی صاحبین کے نزدیک غسل نہیں جائے گا۔
[441] (3) And if a person in a state of janabah (major impurity) is martyred, he should be washed according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and likewise a child. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: They are not washed. [442] (4) And the blood of the martyr is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, but the fur coat, padding, socks, and weapons are removed. [443] (5) And one who survives (al-murtath) is washed. For us (the Hanafis), a junub martyr is washed. According to the two companions (Sahibayn), he is not washed. Their evidence is all those ahadith above that say martyrs should not be washed. Children are sinless just as martyrs are sinless, so the martyr is not washed. By analogy, a child is also not washed according to the Sahibayn.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage covers three sub-rulings related to martyrs. The first (section 441) addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: If a martyr was in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity) at the time of death, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the martyr must be washed because the obligation of ghusl for janabah remains. This is supported by the incident of Hanzalah, whom the angels washed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, arguing that the general rule forbidding washing of martyrs overrides the need for ghusl, and they extend this to a child martyr, drawing an analogy between the child's sinlessness and the martyr's. The second ruling (section 442) states that the martyr's blood is not washed away and his clothes are not removed, except for items that are not suitable for shroud, like leather garments, padded garments, socks, and weapons. The third ruling (section 443) states that a person who survives for some time after being wounded (murtath) is to be washed, as the martyrdom ruling applies only to those who die immediately on the battlefield.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring a full body wash (ghusl).
ارتث (irtaththa): A wounded person who survives the battlefield and later dies, considered a murtath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), how should a martyr who was in a state of janabah be treated?
A) He should be washed because ghusl is obligatory.
B) He should not be washed, just like other martyrs.
C) He should be washed only if he was a child.
D) He should be washed but his clothes should not be removed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa washes a junub martyr, but the mufta bihi position of the Sahibayn is to leave him unwashed.

General Rules for Handling a Martyr's Body: Blood, Clothes, and the Murtath Exception
Rulings on handling a martyr's body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for washing a martyr: that blood is not removed, certain clothes are taken off, and a wounded survivor (murtath) is washed.

Core Idea
A martyr's blood is left, his clothes partially removed, but if he survives the battlefield, he is washed like any ordinary deceased.

Beyond the dispute on janabah, the Hanafi school has clear rules about how a martyr's body is handled: the blood of martyrdom is not washed, and only certain garments are removed. Moreover, if a wounded person survives briefly after the battle, he is considered a murtath and undergoes full washing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sub-rulings
The passage gives three separate rules: blood not washed, clothes partially removed, and murtath washed.
Each rule has its own rationale.
2
Rule 1: Blood not washed
The blood that flows from the martyr's wounds during martyrdom is left as a testimony. It is not washed off.
This symbolizes the sanctity of martyrdom.
3
Rule 2: Clothes partially removed
The martyr's clothes are not removed entirely. However, items not suitable for shroud—like fur coats, padding, socks, and weapons—are taken off.
Leather and weapons are not part of the shroud.
4
Rule 3: Murtath is washed
A murtath is someone who survives the battlefield long enough to be considered not an instant martyr. Such a person is washed and prayed over like any other deceased Muslim.
The instant martyrdom ruling applies only to those who die immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Martyr's Burial: Blood and Clothing Rulings
Ruling on martyr's blood and clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the martyr's blood and clothes and identify which items must be removed before burial.

Core Idea
The martyr is buried with his blood and clothes; only leather, padding, socks, and weapons are removed.

This lesson covers a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding the burial of a martyr who dies on the battlefield. Unlike a regular deceased person, the martyr is not washed and is buried in the clothes he died in, but certain items that are not suitable for the shroud must be removed. This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at the Battle of Uhud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
The passage states: 'The blood of the martyr is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed.' This is the default rule.
This is from the command of the Prophet at Uhud.
2
List Items to Remove
Items that are not part of the normal shroud must be removed: fur coat (farw), padded garment (hashw), leather socks (khuff), and weapons (silah).
These are considered extra and unsuitable for burial.
3
Understand the Evidence
The hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet ordered the removal of iron (weapons) and leather from the martyrs of Uhud and that they be buried with their blood and clothes.
This hadith is from Abu Dawud.
4
Apply the Supplement Rule
If after removing these items the remaining clothing is insufficient for a proper shroud, additional cloth is added to make a standard three-piece shroud.
This ensures the martyr is not buried in insufficient covering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۴٢] ((۴) ولا يغسل عن الشهيد دمه ولا ينزع عنه ثيابه وينزع عنه الفرو والحشو والخف والسلاح
ر شہید کے ساتھ جو کپڑے ہیں اس کو ان کے ساتھ ہی دفن کر دیا جائے گا۔ البتہ جو چیزیں کفن کے لائق نہیں ہیں جیسے چمڑے کا پوستین ، صدری اور کوٹ، چمڑے کے موزے اور ہتھیار ان کو الگ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفن میں کمی رہ جائے تو تین کپڑے کفن کے پورے کئے جائیں گے۔

[442] (4) And the blood of the martyr is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, but the fur coat, padding, socks, and weapons are removed. The martyr is buried with the clothes that are on him. However, things that are not suitable for the shroud, such as leather fur, vest and coat, leather socks, and weapons, these are removed. And if there is a shortage in the shroud, three cloths for the shroud are completed. From Ibn Abbas: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered that the iron and leather be removed from the martyrs of Uhud, and that they be buried with their blood and clothes. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-shahid yughsal, vol. 2 p. 91 no. 3134) From this hadith, it is known that extra items are removed, and the martyr is buried with his clothes. al-farw: leather garment; al-hashw: a garment filled with cotton, coat etc.; al-silah: weapons.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage states the ruling concerning the martyr's blood and clothing. The core principle is that the martyr is buried as is, without washing away the blood and without removing the clothes he was wearing at the time of death. However, items that are not normally part of the shroud—such as leather garments, padded garments (like coats), leather socks, and weapons—must be removed. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered the removal of iron (weapons) and leather from the martyrs of Uhud. If after removing these items the remaining clothing is insufficient for a proper shroud, additional cloth is added to make up the standard three-piece shroud. The text also defines key terms: al-farw (leather garment), al-hashw (padded garment like a coat), and al-silah (weapons). This ruling applies to the martyr who died instantly on the battlefield.

Key Terms
فرو (farw): A leather garment, such as a fur coat.
حشو (hashw): A garment filled with cotton or padding, like a coat or vest.
خف (khuff): Leather socks or boots.
سلاح (silah): Weapons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) A leather coat (farw)
D) Nothing should be removed

Key Takeaway
A martyr is buried with his blood and regular clothes, but leather, padded garments, leather socks, and weapons are removed.

The Murtath: Washing the Battle Survivor
Ruling with proof on washing murtath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that constitute irtithath and state the Hanafi ruling that a murtath must be washed and prayed over.

Core Idea
A wounded fighter who survives and engages in worldly affairs loses the martyr's exemption; he must be washed and prayed over.

In this lesson, we explore a key exception to the martyr's special treatment in funeral rites. The Hanafi school delineates clear conditions under which a battle casualty is considered a 'murtath' (one who survived after being wounded) and thus subject to the full washing and prayer. The ruling is based on the practice of the Companions, as seen in the treatment of Caliph Umar after he was stabbed.

Guided Path
1
Define the Murtath
Identify the legal definition of murtath: a person wounded in battle who survives and engages in worldly activities. List the explicit forms given in the text: eating, drinking, taking medicine, remaining alive conscious until a prayer time passes, or being transferred alive from the battlefield.
2
Extract the Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: such a person is washed, shrouded, and the funeral prayer is performed over him. This is a communal obligation (fard kifayah).
3
Examine the Proof
Analyze the athar of Umar ibn Maymun regarding Caliph Umar. Note that Umar was stabbed, survived for a time, and was later washed and prayed over. This indicates that a person who dies after surviving a battle wound is not treated as an immediate martyr.
The athar is a Qawl Sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the Principle
Grasp the underlying principle: worldly benefit (eating, drinking, etc.) removes the special martyr status. Even if the person is a martyr in the afterlife, the funeral rites are performed because he engaged in the world after his wound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۴۳](۵) ومن ارتث غسل اور ار مثاث کی شکلیں یہ ہیں زخم لگنے کے بعد کھائے، پیئے یا دوا کرائے یا زندہ باقی رہے یہاں تک کہ اس پر ایک نماز کا وقت گزر جائے اس حال میں کہ اس کو ہوش ہو یا میدان جنگ سے زندہ منتقل کیا جائے ۔ تشریح اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ زخم لگنے کے بعد کچھ دیر تک ہوش کی حالت میں زندہ رہا ہو اور دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھایا تو وہ شہید کامل نہیں رہا اس لئے اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا چاہے اخروی اعتبار سے وہ شہید ہو ۔ اب ہوش کے عالم میں تھا اور زخم لگنے کے بعد اس پر نماز کا ایک وقت گزر گیا تو گویا کہ وہ نماز اس کے ذمہ قرض ہو گئی اس لئے یہ بھی دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھانا ہوا اس لئے اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔ ارتثاث والے کو غسل دیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عمر بن ميمون في قصة قتل عمر حين طعنه قال فطار العلج بالسكين ذات طرفين لا يمر على للبيهقي. احد يمينا ولا شمالا الا طعنه وفي ذلك دلالة على انه قتل بمحدد ثم غسل وكفن وصلى عليه (الف) (سنن )
حاشیہ : (ب) عمر بن میمون سے حضرت عمر کے قتل کے سلسلے میں منقول ہے کہ جس وقت ان کو نیزہ مارا، کہ موٹا کا فر دو دھاری چھری لیکر اڑ ادا ئیں بائیں جانب کسی پر بھی نہیں گزرا مگر اس کو نیزہ مارتا چلا گیا۔ اس میں دلالت ہے کہ حضرت عمر تیز دھار والی چیز سے قتل کئے گئے ہیں۔ پھر غسل دیئے گئے ہیں، کفن دیئے گئے ہیں اور ان پر نماز پڑھی گئی۔
[443] (5) And one who survives (al-murtath) is washed. The forms of irtithath (survival) are: after being wounded, he ate, drank, or took medicine, or remained alive until a whole prayer time passed over him while he was conscious, or he was transferred alive from the battlefield. Explanation: The basic rule is that if after being wounded he remained alive for some time in a conscious state and benefited from the world, then he is not a complete martyr, so he is washed, even if in the hereafter he is a martyr. If he was conscious and a full prayer time passed after the wound, then that prayer becomes a debt upon him, so this is also a worldly benefit, thus he is washed. The one who is murtath is washed; its proof is the athar from Umar ibn Maymun concerning the story of the killing of Umar when he was stabbed: he said, 'The uncouth man flew with a double-edged knife, not passing by anyone right or left except that he stabbed him.' In this is evidence that he (Umar) was killed by a sharp object, then he was washed, shrouded, and prayed over. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi)
Footnote: (b) From Umar ibn Maymun concerning the killing of Umar: when he was stabbed, the uncouth man flew with a double-edged knife, not passing by anyone right or left except that he stabbed him. This indicates that Umar was killed by a sharp weapon, then he was washed, shrouded, and prayed over.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage defines the murtath—a person who is wounded in battle but survives for some time after the injury before dying. The ruling is that such a person is treated as a regular deceased: he is washed, shrouded, and the funeral prayer is performed over him. The text explains the conditions that constitute irtithath: eating, drinking, taking medicine, remaining alive until a prayer time passes while conscious, or being moved alive from the battlefield. The underlying principle is that if the person engaged in worldly activities after the injury, the special martyr status (which exempts from washing and prayer) no longer applies. The proof is the incident of Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), who was stabbed but survived for some time, during which he was conscious and likely benefited from worldly matters; he was washed and prayed over after death. Thus, the murtath is not given the full martyr's ruling, even though he may be considered a martyr in the hereafter.

Key Terms
ارتث (irtaththa): A person who is wounded in battle but survives for a period, engaging in worldly activities or remaining conscious, then dies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following would make a wounded person a murtath who must be washed?
A) He dies instantly on the battlefield.
B) He is unconscious for a day and then dies.
C) He eats and drinks after being wounded and then dies later.
D) He is carried away from the battlefield already dead.

Key Takeaway
A murtath is washed and prayed over because he engaged in worldly life after his wound, removing the special martyr's exemption.

Ruling on Washing the Martyr and Removing His Clothes
States the ruling on washing the martyr and removing certain garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing the martyr and identify which items must be removed before burial.

Core Idea
A martyr is not washed, but weapons and leather/fur garments are removed because they are not part of the shroud.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on washing the battlefield martyr. The school holds that the martyr's blood and clothes remain untouched, following the Prophet's practice at Uhud. However, specific items unsuitable for a shroud must be removed. Understanding this distinction is critical for proper burial preparation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: washing the martyr and removing his clothes. The ruling is that the martyr is not washed and his clothes are not removed.
This is the default position; exceptions follow.
2
List the exceptions for removal
Identify which items are removed: the fur coat (farw), padded clothing (hashw), leather socks (khuff), and weapons (silah). All other clothes remain.
These items are not part of the proper shroud for a martyr.
3
Connect to the evidence
The ruling is based on the hadith where the Prophet commanded to bury the martyrs of Uhud with their blood and clothes, removing only iron and leather.
This hadith is transmitted as a single (ahad) narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يغسلان (۴) ولا يغسل عن الشهيد دمه ولا ينزع عنه ثيابه وينزع عنه الفرو والحشو والخف والسلاح
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, do not wash [the martyr]. (4) Nor is the blood of the martyr washed off, nor are his clothes removed; rather, the fur garment, the padded garment, the leather socks, and the weapon are removed from him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the washing of a martyr (shahid). According to Abu Hanifa’s position (which is the basis of the matn), a martyr is not washed at all; his blood is not cleaned, and his clothes are not removed. However, certain items that are not suitable for the shroud (kafan) are removed: the fur coat (farrow), padded clothing (hashw) such as a vest or coat, leather socks (khuff), and weapons (silah). The martyr is buried in his original clothes with his blood as a sign of honor. The proof cited is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet commanded for the martyrs of Uhud to remove iron and leather and bury them with their blood and clothes.

Key Terms
الشهيد (ash-shahid): One who is killed in battle against disbelievers while fighting for Islam, or one who dies in a way that gives him the status of martyrdom.
الفرو (al-farw): A garment made of leather or fur, such as a fur coat.
الحشو (al-hashw): Clothing stuffed with cotton or padding, like a vest or coat.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks typically worn over the feet.
السلاح (as-silah): Weapon, such as a sword, spear, or gun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what items are removed from the martyr before burial?
A) All clothes and blood
B) Fur coat, padded clothing, leather socks, and weapons
C) Only the outer garment
D) Nothing is removed

Key Takeaway
A martyr is not washed and his blood and clothes remain; only fur/padded garments, leather socks, and weapons are removed before burial.

Dispute on Washing a Child Martyr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on washing a child martyr with qiyas reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on washing a child martyr and apply the qiyas reasoning used by the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A child killed in battle is not washed according to the Sahibayn, because innocence from sins parallels the adult martyr.

This passage presents a fascinating dispute within the Hanafi school. While both sides agree on the general rule that adult martyrs are not washed, they differ on children. Abu Hanifa distinguishes the child, while his two students apply qiyas based on the shared attribute of innocence. Understanding this dispute reveals how qiyas khafi operates and how the Sahibayn's view became the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify that Abu Hanifa holds the child should be washed, while the Sahibayn hold it should not be washed. The text refers to 'one view' (Abu Hanifa) and 'the two companions' (Sahibayn).
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on general hadiths commanding that martyrs not be washed, and they draw an analogy (qiyas) between the child and the adult martyr.
The shared attribute (illa) is innocence from sins.
3
Identify the illa of the qiyas
The common effective cause is that both the child and the adult martyr are innocent (ma'sum). Since the adult martyr is not washed due to innocence, the child should also not be washed.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) because the illa is not explicitly stated in the text but derived.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's objection
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the child as not being a 'shahid' in the technical sense—the child is not a fighter who died in battle. Thus the child remains like any other deceased Muslim, who must be washed.
The text does not elaborate on Abu Hanifa's full proof, but his distinction is based on the definition of shahid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn: the child is not washed. This view is preferred as it aligns with the hadiths and is more cautious.
Tarjih authority: the matn presents the Sahibayn's view as correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نزد یک جنبی شہید کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی و تمام احادیث ہے جن میں ہے کہ شہیدوں کو غسل نہ دیا جائے۔ بچے چونکہ گناہوں سے معصوم ہیں جس طرح شہید معصوم ہونگے، اس لئے شہید کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسی پر قیاس کر کے بچے کو بھی صاحبین کے نزدیک غسل نہیں جائے گا۔
According to one view, the martyr (child) will be washed. According to the two companions (Sahibayn), he will not be washed. Their proof is all the hadiths mentioned above that martyrs should not be washed. Because children are innocent of sins just as martyrs are innocent, so the martyr will not be washed. By analogy, the child also, according to the Sahibayn, will not be washed.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a child who is killed in battle. Abu Hanifa's position (referred to as 'one view' in the text) is that such a child should be washed because the child is not a 'shahid' in the full sense? Actually the text says 'nazdik janbi' meaning 'according to one side' – that side is Abu Hanifa. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a child and an adult martyr: a child has no sins, but martyrdom status is specific to adults? The Sahibayn argue that the child is analogous to the martyr because both are innocent, thus the child should not be washed, drawing on the general hadiths that martyrs are not washed. The Hanafi position according to the mufta bihi is that the child martyr is washed? Actually the text says Abu Hanifa's view is to wash, while Sahibayn say no wash. The relied upon position is the view of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) as the matn seems to side with them? The commentary notes that the Sahibayn's proof is the hadiths and qiyas. The dispute shows how qiyas is applied: the effective cause (illa) is innocence from sins, and since both child and martyr share that, the ruling should be the same. Abu Hanifa may consider that the child is not a 'shahid' by definition? The passage does not give his full proof, but it implies his view is based on a distinction.

Key Terms
ارتثاث (irtithath): A wounded person who benefits from worldly means (eats, drinks, receives treatment, or survives through a prayer time in consciousness) before dying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child must be washed
B) The child is not washed
C) It is optional
D) The child is buried without prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that a child killed in battle is not washed, based on qiyas to the adult martyr due to shared innocence.

Ruling on the One Who Benefits from Worldly Things (Irtithath)
Defines irtithath and provides rulings for three categories of deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define irtithath, state the Hanafi ruling that such a person is washed and prayed over, and explain the differing rulings for those killed in hadd/qisas versus rebels.

Core Idea
A wounded person who engages in worldly activities loses full martyrdom status and must be washed.

In this passage, the author defines the term 'irtithath' and clarifies the legal status of a wounded person who benefits from worldly life after receiving a battlefield wound. The Hanafi school rules that such a person is not a shahid kamil and therefore must be washed and the funeral prayer performed over them. The passage also briefly addresses two other categories: those executed for hadd or qisas, who are washed and prayed over, and rebels/highway robbers, over whom prayer is not performed as a deterrent.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition of irtithath
Break down each action listed: eating, drinking, receiving treatment, remaining alive conscious for a full prayer time, or being moved from the battlefield alive.
Any one of these actions suffices to remove shahid status.
2
Identify the legal consequence
The person is not a shahid kamil, so he is washed and the funeral prayer is performed over him.
This is a wajib ruling.
3
Locate the dalil
The practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (ra): after being stabbed, he ate and drank, and then he was washed and prayed over.
This is a Sunnah ahad, zanni in both thubut and dalala.
4
Distinguish from other rulings
Note the additional rulings: those killed in hadd or qisas are also washed and prayed over; rebels and highway robbers are not prayed over.
The difference reflects the level of sin and deterrence.
5
Understand the wisdom
Irtithath indicates benefit from dunia, so he is treated as a regular deceased. Not praying over rebels serves as a deterrent.
These are established Hanafi positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والارتشاث ان يأكل او يشرب او يداوي او يبقى حيا حتى يمضى عليه وقت صلوة وهو يعقل وينقل من المعركة حيا (۶) ومن قتل في حد او قصاص غسل و صلی علیه (۷) ومن قتل من البغاة او قطاع الطريق لم يصل عليه.
And irtithath is that he eats or drinks or receives treatment or remains alive until a prayer time passes over him while he is conscious, and he is moved from the battlefield alive. (6) And whoever is killed in a hadd or qisas punishment, he is washed and prayed over. (7) And whoever is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, prayer is not performed over him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'irtithath' (ارتثاث). A wounded person who, after receiving his wound, eats, drinks, uses medicine, or remains alive conscious through one full prayer time, or is taken alive from the battlefield, is considered to have benefited from worldly life. Such a person does not have the full status of a martyr (shahid kamil) and therefore must be washed (ghusl) and the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is performed over him. The proof cited is the story of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who after being stabbed ate and drank, and he was washed and prayed upon. The passage also transitions into two other rulings: (6) Anyone executed for a fixed punishment (hadd) or retaliation (qisas) is washed and prayed over because they are believers, even if they died as sinners. (7) Rebels (baghi) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) are not prayed over as a deterrent and to show disapproval of their actions. The hadith of the man who committed suicide is cited as evidence for not praying over such people.

Key Terms
ارتثاث (irtithath): The condition of a wounded person who engages in worldly activities after being wounded, which removes the full martyrdom status.
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft).
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliatory punishment for murder or injury.
باغي (baghi): Rebel against a legitimate Muslim ruler.
قاطع طريق (qati' tariq): Highway robber or bandit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an action that constitutes irtithath?
A) Eating
B) Drinking
C) Killing an enemy
D) Receiving medical treatment

Key Takeaway
A wounded person who benefits from worldly life (irtithath) loses full martyrdom status and must be washed and prayed over, while rebels are not prayed over as a deterrent.

The Murtath: Wounded Warrior Who Benefits from the World
Ruling on the murtath (wounded warrior who benefits from world after injury)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criteria for a murtath and explain why ghusl is required for them.

Core Idea
A murtath is not a martyr; he receives full funeral rites because he partook of worldly benefits after injury.

In this passage, we learn about the category of a 'murtath' – a wounded soldier who remains alive and benefits from worldly sustenance. The ruling distinguishes him from a battlefield martyr, requiring full washing and funeral prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the text to find the conditions that classify a wounded person as murtath: eating, drinking, treatment, or remaining conscious past a prayer time.
2
Understand the ruling
The murtath receives ghusl and funeral prayer because he is not a true martyr; his worldly actions remove the martyr's privileges.
3
Examine the proof
The incident of Umar (RA) is cited: after being stabbed, he ate and drank, so he was given ghusl. This illustrates the criterion.

والارتشاف ان يأكل او يشرب او يداوي او يبقى حيا حتى يمضى عليه وقت صلوة وهو يعقل وينقل من المعركة حيا (۴۴۴) (۲) ومن قتل في حد او قصاص غسل و صلی علیه (۴۴۵) (۷) ومن قتل من البغاة او قطاع الطريق لم يصل عليه. اس اثر میں حضرت عمر کو زخم لگنے کے بعد انہوں نے کھایا پیا ہے، اس لئے ان کو نسل دیا گیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زخم لگنے کے بعد جس نے دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھایا اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔ (۴۴۴) (۶) جو حد قصاص میں قتل کیا گیا اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ غسل تو اس لئے دیا جائے گا کہ وہ شہید نہیں ہے بلکہ عام میت کی طرح ہے۔ اور نماز اس لئے پڑھی جائے گی کہ یہ مؤمن ہے (۲) حضرت ماعز اسلمی جو حد میں قتل ہوئے تھے ان پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی گئی تھی ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی من قبلہ الحدودج ثانی ص ۹۸ نمبر ۳۱۸۶) (۳) جہینہ کی عورت زنا کی حد میں رجم کی گئی تو آپ نے اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی عن عبد الـلـه بـن بــريــدة عن ابيه في قصة الغامدية التي رجمت في الزنا قال النبي الا الله والذي نفسي بيده لقد تابت توبة لو تابها صاحب مكس لغفر له ثم امر لها فصلى عليها و دفنت (الف) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب الصلوة على من قبلہ الحدودج رابع ص ۲۵، نمبر ۶۸۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم للبيهقى ہوا کہ حد میں قتل ہونے پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی۔ ۴۴۵] (۷) اگر باغیوں میں سے قتل کیا گیا ہو یاڈاکؤوں سے قتل کیا گیا ہوتو اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ تا کہ لوگوں کو تنبیہ ہو کہ ایسا کرنے سے نماز جنازہ سے بھی محروم ہو جاتے ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر بن سمرة قال اتی النبی لله به رجل قتل نفسه بمشاقص فلم يصل عليه (ب) (سنن بیھقی ، باب الصلوة على من قتل نفسه غير مستحل لقتلهاج رابع ص ۲۹ نمبر ۶۸۳۳) اس حدیث میں اپنے کو قتل کرنے والے پر حضور نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تو اسی طرح ڈاکؤوں اور باغیوں پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے چونکہ میت مومن ہے اس لئے اور لوگ نماز پڑھ لیں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) غامدیہ کے سلسلے میں روایت ہے جو زنا کے سلسلے میں رجم کی گئی۔ آپ نے فرمایا تم اس ذات کی جس کے قبضہ میں میری جان ہے ایسی توبہ کی کہ اگر چنگی وصول کرنے والا ایسی توبہ کرے تو اللہ اس کو معاف کر دے۔ پھر حکم دیا گیا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی گئی اور دفن کی گئی (ب) حضور کے سامنے ایسا آدمی لایا گیا کہ اس نے اپنے آپ کو چھری سے قتل کیا تھا تو آپ نے اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی۔
And the one who eats, drinks, or receives treatment, or remains alive until the time of prayer passes while he is conscious and is moved from the battlefield alive: (444) (2) Whoever is killed in a hadd or qisas punishment, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered over him. (445) (7) Whoever is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, no prayer is offered over him. This narration indicates that after Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) was injured, he ate and drank, so he was given ghusl. It is learned that one who benefits from the world after injury is given ghusl. (444) (6) Whoever is killed in hadd or qisas, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered over him. Ghusl is given because he is not a martyr but is like an ordinary deceased person. Prayer is offered because he is a believer. (2) Ma'iz al-Aslami, who was killed in a hadd, funeral prayer was offered over him (Abu Dawood, chapter on prayer over those upon whom hadd is carried out, vol. 2 p. 98 no. 3186). (3) A woman from Juhaynah was stoned for the hadd of zina, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) offered funeral prayer over her. 'Abdullah ibn Buraydah narrated from his father regarding the story of al-Ghamidiyyah who was stoned for zina: The Prophet said, 'By the One in whose hand is my soul, she has repented such that if a tax collector were to repent like that, he would be forgiven.' Then he ordered for her, prayed over her, and she was buried. (Narrated by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over those upon whom hadd is carried out, vol. 4 p. 25 no. 6820). From this hadith it is learned that funeral prayer is offered over one killed in a hadd. (445) (7) If someone is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, no prayer is offered over him, as a warning to people that doing such deeds deprives them of funeral prayer. There is a hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah: A man who killed himself with a sharp arrow was brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he did not pray over him (narrated by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over one who commits suicide without deeming it lawful, vol. 4 p. 29 no. 6833). In this hadith, the Prophet did not pray over the suicide, so similarly no prayer is offered over robbers and rebels. However, since the deceased is a believer, other people may offer the prayer. Footnote: (a) There is a narration about al-Ghamidiyyah who was stoned for zina. He said, 'By the One in whose hand is my soul, she has repented such that if a tax collector were to repent like that, Allah would forgive him.' Then he ordered and prayer was offered over her and she was buried. (b) A man was brought before the Prophet who had killed himself with a knife, and he did not pray over him.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) from Al-Sharh al-Samarqandi on the chapter of prayer. It addresses the rulings on washing (ghusl) and funeral prayer (janazah) for three categories: the one gravely wounded in battle (al-murtath), one killed in hudud or qisas, and rebels/bandits. The author first mentions the murtath: if after injury he eats, drinks, or receives treatment, or remains alive past a prayer time while conscious, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered—because he is not a true martyr of the battlefield. The proof is the incident of Umar (RA), who after being stabbed ate and drank, and was given ghusl. Next, the one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retributive justice (qisas): he is given ghusl because he is not a martyr, and prayer is offered because he is a believer. This is supported by the hadith of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah where the Prophet (SAW) prayed over them. Then, for rebels (baghi) and highway robbers: no funeral prayer is offered over them as a deterrent. The analogy is made to the hadith of the man who committed suicide, upon whom the Prophet did not pray. The text notes that despite the prohibition, other Muslims may pray for them since they are believers. The footnote repeats the two hadiths in Arabic with references. The overall ruling according to the Hanafi madhhab is that those killed in hadd or qisas receive full funeral rites, while rebels and robbers are denied the public funeral prayer as a punishment and deterrent.

Key Terms
مرتث (murtath): One who is gravely wounded in battle but remains alive and partakes of worldly benefits (food/drink/treatment) before dying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Eating or drinking after injury
B) Receiving medical treatment
C) Remaining conscious past a full prayer time
D) Dying instantly on the battlefield

Key Takeaway
A wounded soldier who partakes of worldly benefits after injury is a murtath and must receive full funeral rites.

Funeral Rites for Those Killed in Hadd or Qisas
Ruling on funeral rites for those killed in hadd or qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl and funeral prayer for those executed in hadd or qisas and cite the prophetic proof.

Core Idea
Those killed in hadd or qisas are believers, not martyrs; they receive full funeral rites.

This lesson examines the ruling for individuals executed under prescribed punishments (hadd) or retributive justice (qisas). The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice, holds that such persons are washed and prayed over, affirming their faith while denying them the special status of martyrs.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text clearly says: 'Whoever is killed in a hadd or qisas punishment, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered over him.'
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Understand the rationale
Ghusl is given because they are not martyrs; prayer is offered because they are still believers despite sin.
Martyrdom (shahada) is reserved for those killed unjustly in battle, not as a punishment.
3
Examine the proofs
The Prophet (SAW) prayed over Ma'iz al-Aslami (stoned for zina) and over al-Ghamidiyyah. These hadiths establish the ruling.
Narrations from Abu Dawood and al-Bayhaqi are cited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(445) (7) Whoever is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, no prayer is offered over him. This narration indicates that after Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) was injured, he ate and drank, so he was given ghusl. It is learned that one who benefits from the world after injury is given ghusl. (444) (6) Whoever is killed in hadd or qisas, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered over him. Ghusl is given because he is not a martyr but is like an ordinary deceased person. Prayer is offered because he is a believer. (2) Ma'iz al-Aslami, who was killed in a hadd, funeral prayer was offered over him (Abu Dawood, chapter on prayer over those upon whom hadd is carried out, vol. 2 p. 98 no. 3186). (3) A woman from Juhaynah was stoned for the hadd of zina, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) offered funeral prayer over her. 'Abdullah ibn Buraydah narrated from his father regarding the story of al-Ghamidiyyah who was stoned for zina: The Prophet said, 'By the One in whose hand is my soul, she has repented such that if a tax collector were to repent like that, he would be forgiven.' Then he ordered for her, prayed over her, and she was buried. (Narrated by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over those upon whom hadd is carried out, vol. 4 p. 25 no. 6820). From this hadith it is learned that funeral prayer is offered over one killed in a hadd. (445) (7) If someone is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, no prayer is offered over him, as a warning to people that doing such deeds deprives them of funeral prayer. There is a hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah: A man who killed himself with a sharp arrow was brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he did not pray over him (narrated by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over one who commits suicide without deeming it lawful, vol. 4 p. 29 no. 6833). In this hadith, the Prophet did not pray over the suicide, so similarly no prayer is offered over robbers and rebels. However, since the deceased is a believer, other people may offer the prayer. Footnote: (a) There is a narration about al-Ghamidiyyah who was stoned for zina. He said, 'By the One in whose hand is my soul, she has repented such that if a tax collector were to repent like that, Allah would forgive him.' Then he ordered and prayer was offered over her and she was buried. (b) A man was brought before the Prophet who had killed himself with a knife, and he did not pray over him.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) from Al-Sharh al-Samarqandi on the chapter of prayer. It addresses the rulings on washing (ghusl) and funeral prayer (janazah) for three categories: the one gravely wounded in battle (al-murtath), one killed in hudud or qisas, and rebels/bandits. The author first mentions the murtath: if after injury he eats, drinks, or receives treatment, or remains alive past a prayer time while conscious, he is given ghusl and prayer is offered—because he is not a true martyr of the battlefield. The proof is the incident of Umar (RA), who after being stabbed ate and drank, and was given ghusl. Next, the one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retributive justice (qisas): he is given ghusl because he is not a martyr, and prayer is offered because he is a believer. This is supported by the hadith of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah where the Prophet (SAW) prayed over them. Then, for rebels (baghi) and highway robbers: no funeral prayer is offered over them as a deterrent. The analogy is made to the hadith of the man who committed suicide, upon whom the Prophet did not pray. The text notes that despite the prohibition, other Muslims may pray for them since they are believers. The footnote repeats the two hadiths in Arabic with references. The overall ruling according to the Hanafi madhhab is that those killed in hadd or qisas receive full funeral rites, while rebels and robbers are denied the public funeral prayer as a punishment and deterrent.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A prescribed punishment for crimes like fornication, theft, etc., fixed by Allah.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice, typically in cases of murder or injury, equal punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Prophet's prayer over Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah
C) The Quranic verse on forgiveness

Key Takeaway
Those killed in hadd or qisas are believers; the Prophet's prayer over them establishes the obligation of funeral rites.

Denying Funeral Prayer to Rebels and Highway Robbers
Ruling on funeral prayer for rebels and robbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer for rebels and highway robbers and explain the deterrent rationale.

Core Idea
No public funeral prayer for rebels and robbers, as a deterrent; private prayer is allowed.

The passage now turns to two categories: rebels (baghah) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq). The Hanafi school denies them the public funeral prayer as a punishment for their sins and a warning to others, though private individuals may still pray for them. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Prophet's treatment of a suicide.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text says: 'Whoever is killed among the rebels or highway robbers, no prayer is offered over him.'
This refers to the public, official prayer led by the imam.
2
Understand the rationale
The purpose is deterrence: to discourage others from committing such crimes by depriving them of the honor of a public funeral prayer.
The deceased still had faith; private prayer by individuals is permissible.
3
Examine the proof
The Prophet (SAW) did not pray over a man who committed suicide. Analogy (qiyas) is made: suicides, rebels, and robbers all commit major sins deserving public denouncement.
The hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah is cited.

Prayer Inside the Kaaba: Rulings and Conditions
Rules for salah inside the Kaaba individually and in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside the Kaaba and apply the orientation rules for congregational prayer, identifying which positions are valid, makruh, or invalid.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid; but in congregation, the follower must not be ahead of the imam.

This lesson examines the unique situation of praying inside the sacred House of Allah. While the Kaaba is the direction of prayer, inside it there is no conventional 'front' direction. The Hanafi school holds that such prayer is valid for both fard and nafl, based on the Prophet's practice. However, when praying in congregation, special care must be taken with orientation to maintain the rule that a follower must not be ahead of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage rules on two acts: (1) individual prayer inside the Kaaba (valid), and (2) congregational prayer inside the Kaaba (valid with conditions). Note the hukm level: sahih (valid) for both, but with restrictions for congregation.
The individual ruling is general; the congregational ruling depends on follower orientation.
2
Locate the dalil for individual prayer
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar in Sahih al-Bukhari: the Prophet (SAW) prayed inside the Kaaba between two front pillars. This action is explicit evidence (dalil naqli) that prayer inside is permissible.
Thubut is qati (authentic), dalala is zanni (the precise orientation is inferred).
3
Analyze the three congregational orientations
The text describes three positions of followers relative to the imam: (1) back to imam's back – valid; (2) face to imam's face – valid but makruh; (3) back to imam's face – invalid. Each must be evaluated against the rule that a follower must not be ahead of the imam.
The key principle: the follower's location relative to the imam, not the direction they face.
4
Apply the general rule of follower not ahead of imam
In case (1) the follower is behind the imam (since both face outward). In case (2) the follower is also not ahead (faces imam but remains behind). In case (3) the follower's back to imam's face means the follower is physically ahead of the imam, violating the rule.
This is a qiyas: the general rule of salat al-jama'ah is applied to the unique setting inside the Kaaba.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling: prayer inside the Kaaba is valid individually and in congregation, provided no follower is placed ahead of the imam. Facing the imam's face is makruh tanzihi (disliked), not haram.
This is the standard Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلوة في الكعبة [۴۴۶ (۱) الصلوة فى الكعبة جائزة فرضها ونقلها ۴۴۷ (۲) فان صلى الامام فيها بجماعة فجعل بعضهم ظهره الى ظهر الامام جاز ([۴۴۸(۳) ومن جعل منهم وجهه الى وجه الامام طاز ويكره [۴۴۹] (۴) ومن جعل منهم ظهره الى وجه الامام لم تجز صلوته. ضروری نوٹ بیت اللہ کے اندر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بیت اللہ کا کچھ نہ کچھ حصہ سامنے ہوگا جو قبلہ ہو جائے گا۔ اور قبلہ بننے کے لئے اتنا کافی ہے۔ باقی دلائل آگے آرہے ہیں۔ (۴۴۶) (۱) کعبہ میں نماز جائز ہے، فرض بھی اور نفل بھی۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال دخل النبي الله الله البيت واسامة بن زيد و عثمان بن طلحه و بلال فاطال ثم خرج وكنت اول الناس دخل على اثره فسألت بلالا این صلى فقال بين العمودين المقدمين (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة بين السواری فی غیر جماعۃ ، کتاب الصلوۃ ، ص ۷۲ نمبر ۵۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیت اللہ کے اندر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ۱۴۴۷ (۲) اگر امام نے بیت اللہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی اور بعض نے اپنی پیٹھے امام کی پیٹھ کی طرف کی تو نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ مقتدی نے اپنی پیٹھ امام کی پیٹھ کی طرف کر لی تو مقتدی امام کے آگے نہیں ہوا بلکہ امام کی پیچھے ہی رہا، اور مقتدی کے سامنے بھی قبلہ موجود ہے اس لئے نماز ہو جائے گی۔ [۴۴۸] (۳) اور جس مقتدی نے اپنا چہرہ امام کے چہرہ کی طرف کیا تو بھی نماز جائز ہوگی لیکن مکروہ ہوگی۔ اس صورت میں بھی امام کے چہرے کی طرف مقتدی کی پیٹھ نہیں ہوئی اس لئے نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن امام کے چہرہ کی طرف چہرہ کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ [۴۴۹ (۴) مقتدی میں سے جس نے اپنی پیٹھے امام کے چہرہ کی طرف کی اس کی نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ امام کے چہرہ کی طرف مقتدی کی پیٹھ ہوگئی تو مقتدی امام کے بالکل آگے ہو گیا اور پہلے قاعدہ گزر گیا ہے کہ مقتدی امام کے آگے ہو جائے تو مقتدی کی نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ یہ مسئلہ قاعدہ پر مستقبط ہے۔ اوپر کی چار شکلیں بیت اللہ کے اندر نماز پڑھنے کی ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ بیت اللہ میں داخل ہوئے اور اسامہ بن زید اور عثمان بن طلحہ اور بلال داخل ہوئے پھر نکلے۔ تو میں سب سے پہلے ان کے پیچھے داخل ہوا اور حضرت بلال سے پوچھا کہ کہاں نماز پڑھی تو فرمایا کہ اگلے دوستونوں کے درمیان۔
Chapter of Prayer in the Kaaba. [446] (1) Prayer in the Kaaba is valid, both obligatory and supererogatory. [447] (2) If the Imam prays in it with a congregation, and some of them make their backs towards the back of the Imam, it is valid. [448] (3) And whoever among them makes his face towards the face of the Imam, it is valid but disliked (makruh). [449] (4) And whoever among them makes his back towards the face of the Imam, his prayer is not valid. Necessary note: It is valid to pray inside the Kaaba because some part of the Kaaba will be in front, which becomes the qibla. And that is sufficient for the qibla. The remaining evidences are coming ahead. (446) (1) Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid, both fard and nafl. There is a hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet entered the House with Usama bin Zaid, Uthman bin Talha, and Bilal, and he prolonged [the prayer], then came out. I was the first of people to enter after him, and I asked Bilal where he prayed. He said, 'Between the two front pillars.' (Al-Bukhari, chapter on prayer between pillars without congregation, book of prayer, p. 72, no. 504). From this hadith it is learned that prayer inside the Kaaba is valid. (447) (2) If the Imam prays in the Kaaba with a congregation, and some of them make their backs towards the back of the Imam, the prayer is valid. The follower made his back towards the back of the Imam, so the follower is not ahead of the Imam but remains behind the Imam, and in front of the follower the qibla is present, so the prayer is valid. (448) (3) And whoever among the followers made his face towards the face of the Imam, the prayer is valid but disliked. In this case also, the follower's back is not towards the Imam's face, so the prayer is valid. But facing the Imam's face is not good, therefore it is makruh. (449) (4) And whoever among the followers made his back towards the face of the Imam, his prayer is not valid. The follower's back becomes towards the Imam's face, so the follower becomes completely ahead of the Imam, and the earlier rule has passed that if the follower becomes ahead of the Imam, the follower's prayer is not valid. This issue is based on the rule. The four forms above are for praying inside the Kaaba. Footnote: (a) He entered the Kaaba with Usama bin Zaid, Uthman bin Talha, and Bilal, then came out. I was the first to enter after them, and I asked Bilal where he prayed, and he said, 'Between the two front pillars.'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) from the commentary on the chapter of prayer inside the Kaaba. The author begins by affirming that praying inside the Kaaba is valid for both fard and nafl prayers. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (SAW) prayed inside the Kaaba between the two front pillars. The author then explains the conditions for congregational prayer inside the Kaaba, detailing three possible orientations of the followers relative to the imam: (1) If the follower turns his back to the imam's back, the prayer is valid because the follower remains behind the imam (even though they face different walls) and faces a part of the Kaaba as qibla. (2) If the follower faces the imam (i.e., they face each other), the prayer is valid but makruh (disliked) because it is not proper to face the imam directly, even though the follower is still behind the imam in a sense. (3) If the follower turns his back to the imam's face (i.e., the follower stands with his back towards the imam's front), the prayer is invalid because the follower is effectively ahead of the imam, which is prohibited in Hanafi fiqh (a follower must not stand ahead of the imam). The footnote reiterates the hadith evidence. This ruling is specific to the unique situation of praying inside the Kaaba, where directions are unconventional. The overall ruling according to the Hanafi school is that prayer inside the Kaaba is valid, and congregation is permissible with specific orientation rules to avoid the follower being ahead of the imam.

Key Terms
کعبہ (Kaaba): The sacred House of Allah in Mecca, the direction of prayer (qibla) for all Muslims.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer, who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prayer invalid if a follower turns his back to the imam's face inside the Kaaba?
A) Because the follower is no longer facing the Kaaba.
B) Because the follower becomes ahead of the imam, which is prohibited.
C) Because it is makruh to face away from the imam.
D) Because the imam's prayer is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid individually; congregational prayer is valid as long as no follower is physically ahead of the imam.

Prayer Inside the Kaaba is Valid
Ruling on permissibility with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside the Kaaba and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid; facing any part suffices for qibla.

This chapter addresses a specific question: can one pray inside the Kaaba itself? The Hanafi school affirms that it is permissible, whether the prayer is obligatory or voluntary. The proof comes from the Sunnah: the Prophet himself prayed inside the Kaaba between the two front pillars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying inside the Kaaba. The ruling is that it is permissible and valid for both obligatory and voluntary prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet entered the Kaaba and prayed between the two front pillars.
Hadith reference: Bukhari, Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Salah bayna al-Sawari fi Ghayr Jama'ah, no. 504.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action demonstrates permissibility. The specific location between pillars shows that facing any part of the Kaaba is sufficient for qibla.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The source indicates that this ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the schools. No significant dispute is mentioned.
