Follower's Back to Imam's Back Inside Kaaba
Ruling and its commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a follower inside the Kaaba makes his back towards the imam's back and explain why it is valid based on the conditions of muqtadi and qibla.

Core Idea
A follower must not be ahead of the imam; facing away from him is valid if qibla is before the follower.

Inside the Kaaba, the spatial arrangement of congregational prayer can be unusual. This lesson examines a specific case: when a follower turns his back to the imam's back. By understanding the Hanafi conditions—that the follower must be behind the imam and facing the qibla—you will see why this scenario remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a congregational prayer inside the Kaaba where some followers orient themselves with their backs towards the imam's back. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (ja'iz).
The ruling is explicitly stated in the matn.
2
Identify the condition: follower is behind the imam
The commentator explains that by turning his back to the imam's back, the follower does not become ahead of the imam; he remains behind him. This satisfies the condition that the muqtadi must not be ahead of the imam.
In Hanafi fiqh, being at the same level or behind is permissible; ahead invalidates the prayer.
3
Identify the condition: follower faces the qibla
Even though the follower faces away from the imam, he still faces some part of the Kaaba structure, which is the qibla. This fulfills the condition of facing the qibla.
Inside the Kaaba, any direction inside the structure is considered facing the qibla.
4
Conclude the ruling
Since both conditions are met (behind the imam and facing the qibla), the prayer is valid. No additional alignment with the imam's front is required.

If the imam prays in the House of Allah with a congregation, and some make their back towards the back of the imam, then the prayer will be valid. The follower made his back to the back of the imam, so the follower did not become ahead of the imam, but remained behind him. Also, the qibla is in front of the follower, so the prayer will be valid.

This is a ruling on the validity of congregational prayer inside the Kaaba when the follower positions himself with his back towards the imam's back. The commentator explains that in this scenario, the follower is not ahead of the imam—he remains behind him—and he is still facing the qibla (some part of the Kaaba), so the prayer is valid.

Follower Faces Imam: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on validity and dislike of follower facing imam's face inside Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a follower facing the imam's face inside the Kaaba and explain why it is considered makruh.

Core Idea
Facing the imam's face is makruh but does not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario inside the Kaaba where a follower directly faces the imam. The text rules the prayer valid because the follower's back is not towards the imam, but it also declares the act disliked. Understanding this distinction helps avoid confusion between valid actions and those that are merely discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is a follower making his face towards the imam's face during prayer inside the Kaaba. The ruling is that the prayer is valid but disliked.
The validity is because the follower's back is not towards the imam; the dislike is because facing the imam's face is not good.
2
Analyze the condition for validity
The key condition for validity is that the follower's back must not be towards the imam, which would place him ahead. Here, facing the imam's face ensures the back is not towards him.
3
Understand the dislike (makruh)
The dislike is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not makruh tahrimi. It does not affect validity but is not recommended.
In Hanafi fiqh, makruh tanzihi is close to halal and does not incur sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[448] (3) And whoever among them makes his face towards the face of the imam is permissible [but] disliked. The follower who makes his face towards the imam's face, then the prayer will still be valid, but it will be disliked. In this situation, the follower's back is not towards the imam's face, so the prayer will be valid. However, facing the imam's face is not good, so it is disliked.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This ruling addresses the situation where a follower inside the Kaaba faces the imam directly (face to face). The prayer is still valid because the follower's back is not towards the imam (which would make him ahead). However, facing the imam's face is considered not good and is disliked (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked and not recommended, but not sinful. In Hanafi, it can be tanzihi (lighter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Follower Behind Imam: When a Follower Turns His Back to the Imam

Core Idea
If a follower is ahead of the imam, even by turning his back, the prayer is invalid.

This lesson examines a specific application of the general rule that a follower must not be ahead of the imam. The text considers a scenario inside the Kaaba where the follower's back faces the imam, making him ahead. Understanding this helps reinforce the condition of following the imam in congregational prayer.

Identify the scenario

Apply the rule

Validity of Follower Closer to Kaaba than Imam in Masjid al-Haram
Ruling on follower proximity in circular congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a follower who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam in Masjid al-Haram has a valid prayer.

Core Idea
Following the imam means staying behind his direction, not behind a physical structure.

This lesson examines a unique scenario in the Masjid al-Haram where the congregation surrounds the Kaaba. The imam's position relative to the Kaaba and the followers' positions creates a question: if a follower is physically closer to the Kaaba than the imam, does that make him 'in front'? The Hanafi answer distinguishes based on which side of the imam the follower stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying in congregation behind an imam in Masjid al-Haram. The ruling is that the prayer is valid unless a specific condition is violated.
The base ruling is permissibility.
2
Distinguish the two cases
The source text presents two scenarios: a follower on the imam's side versus a follower on a different side. On the same side, being closer to the Kaaba puts the follower ahead; on other sides, it does not.
The key factor is the follower's direction relative to the imam.
3
Apply the condition
The condition for validity is that the follower must not be on the imam's side if he is closer to the Kaaba. If he is on a different side, his prayer is valid.
This condition prevents the follower from being ahead of the imam in the direction of prayer.
4
Explain the rationale
Being closer to the Kaaba on the same side as the imam means the follower is physically in front of the imam, which breaks the required alignment. On other sides, proximity to the Kaaba does not place the follower ahead of the imam's line of prayer.
The ruling preserves the principle that followers must not precede the imam in positioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۵۰ (۵) واذا صلى الامام في المسجد الحرام تحلق الناس حول الكعبة وصلوا بصلوة الامام فمن كان منهم اقرب الى الكعبة من الامام جازت صلوته اذا لم يكن في جانب الامام
اگر مسجد حرام میں نماز پڑھائے اور سب لوگ کعبہ کے ارد گرد حلقہ بنائے اور امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تو جوان میں سے کعبہ سے زیادہ قریب ہو امام سے بھی تو اس کی نماز جائز ہے جب کہ امام کی جانب نہ ہو۔
امام کی جانب جو لوگ ہو اور امام سے بھی زیادہ بیت اللہ کے قریب ہو جائے تو امام کی جانب امام سے بھی آگے ہو جائے ئیں گے اس لئے اس آدمی کی نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ اور جو لوگ امام کی جانب نہیں ہیں دوسری جانب ہیں وہ لوگ اگر کعبہ کے زیادہ قریب ہو گئے تو چونکہ وہ امام کی جانب نہیں ہیں اس لئے امام سے آگے نہیں ہوئے اس لئے ان کی نماز ہو جائے گی۔
[450] (5) And if the imam prays in the Masjid al-Haram, and the people circle around the Kaaba and pray with the imam's prayer, then whoever among them is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, his prayer is valid, if he is not on the side of the imam. If the imam leads prayer in the Masjid al-Haram and all people form a circle around the Kaaba and pray with the imam, then whoever among them is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, his prayer is valid, provided he is not on the imam's side. Those who are on the imam's side and become closer to the Kaaba than the imam, they become ahead of the imam on his side, so their prayer is not valid. As for those who are not on the imam's side but on other sides, even if they become closer to the Kaaba, since they are not on the imam's side, they do not become ahead of the imam, so their prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This ruling deals with congregational prayer in the Masjid al-Haram where the imam is located and followers circle around the Kaaba. If a follower is on the same side as the imam and is closer to the Kaaba, he becomes ahead of the imam, invalidating his prayer. But if he is on a different side, being closer does not put him ahead of the imam, so his prayer is valid.

Key Terms
مسجد الحرام (Masjid al-Haram): The Grand Mosque in Makkah surrounding the Kaaba.
جانب الامام (janib al-imam): The side of the imam; the direction in which the imam faces (toward the Kaaba).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Masjid al-Haram, if a follower is on the imam's side and closer to the Kaaba, what is the ruling?
A) His prayer is valid.
B) His prayer is invalid.
C) His prayer is valid but disliked.
D) His prayer is invalid only if the imam is on the same side.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prayer in Masjid al-Haram is valid if closer to the Kaaba but not on the imam's side.

Prayer on the Roof of the Kaaba: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on prayer on Kaaba roof with validity and dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on the roof of the Kaaba and explain the concept of muḥādhāt (airspace) as sufficient for the qibla condition.

Core Idea
Prayer on the Kaaba roof is valid because its airspace is qibla, but it is disliked for disrespect.

This short passage touches on a subtle point: the physical structure of the Kaaba versus its sacred airspace. The Hanafi school holds that the qibla condition is satisfied by the airspace directly above the Kaaba (muḥādhāt), not solely its walls. This ruling also provides the foundation for understanding why prayer in an airplane is valid when flying over the Kaaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Primary Ruling
The act is praying on the 'back' (roof) of the Kaaba. The text begins by stating the prayer is valid (jāza). Determine the primary hukm: sahih (valid).
Validity here means the prayer fulfills its essential conditions and pillars.
2
Identify the Secondary Ruling: Dislike
The text adds that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) because it contradicts the honor and grandeur of the Kaaba. This does not affect validity, but it indicates a lower reward.
Makruh tanzihi is close to halal but discouraged.
3
Understand the Qibla Principle: Muḥādhāt (Airspace)
The reason for validity is that the airspace directly above the Kaaba (muḥādhāt) is considered 'facing the qibla'. The text explicitly says it is not necessary to have the wall of the Kaaba in front; its airspace suffices.
This principle is unique to the Hanafi school among the four.
4
Apply the Principle to Real Cases
The text provides the airplane analogy: a person in an airplane above Makkah does not see the Kaaba walls, yet the prayer is valid because the airspace aligns with the qibla.
This shows the practicality of muḥādhāt in modern travel.
5
Note the Hadith Context
A hadith is cited forbidding prayer in seven places (garbage dump, slaughterhouse, etc.). The roof of the Kaaba is not among those prohibited places, so the prayer is not invalid. However, it is still disliked due to respect.
The hadith is cut off in the text; only the beginning is quoted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۵۱ (٦) ومن صلى على ظهر الكعبة جازت صلوته
جس نے بیت اللہ کی چھت پر نماز پڑھی اس کی نماز جائز ہے۔ بیت اللہ کی چھت پر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ اس کی شان اور عظمت کے خلاف ہے۔ لیکن اگر پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ بیت اللہ کی محاذات کی فضا اس کے سامنے ہوگی جو قبلہ ہو جائے گی۔ قبلہ ہونے کے لئے بیت اللہ کی دیوار سامنے ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی فضا سامنے ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جیسے کوئی ہوائی جہاز میں نماز پڑھے تو جہاز کی بلندی کی وجہ سے بیت اللہ کی دیوار اس کے سامنے نہیں ہوگی۔ صرف بیت اللہ کے محاذات کی فضا اس کے سامنے ہوگی اور نماز ہو جائے گی۔ بیت اللہ کے اوپر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر ان النبي صلى الله عليه نهى ان يصلى في سبعة مواطن في المزبلة والمجزرة والمقبرة وقارعة الطريق وفي الحمام
[451] (6) And whoever prays on the back (roof) of the Kaaba, his prayer is valid. Whoever prays on the roof of the House of Allah, his prayer is valid. Praying on the roof of the House of Allah is disliked because it is against its honor and grandeur. But if he prays, the prayer will be valid. Because the airspace directly above the Kaaba will be in front of him, which becomes the qibla. For the qibla, it is not necessary to have the wall of the Kaaba in front; rather, its airspace in front is necessary. For example, if someone prays in an airplane, due to the height, the wall of the Kaaba will not be in front of him; only the airspace above the Kaaba will be in front, and the prayer will be valid. Praying on top of the Kaaba is disliked. Its proof is the hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade praying in seven places: the garbage dump, the slaughterhouse, the graveyard, the middle of the road, and in the bathroom...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This ruling addresses prayer on the roof (top) of the Kaaba. The prayer is valid because the airspace above the Kaaba suffices as qibla; one does not need the actual wall. However, it is disliked (makruh) due to disrespect to the Kaaba's honor. The commentator cites a hadith forbidding prayer in certain places, implying the roof is not among them, but the act is disliked for reverence.

Key Terms
محاذات (muḥādhāt): The space directly above or in line with an object. Here it refers to the airspace above the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying on the roof of the Kaaba according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is invalid because one cannot face the qibla properly.
B) It is valid and recommended.
C) It is valid but disliked.
D) It is only valid for voluntary prayers.

Key Takeaway
Prayer on the roof of the Kaaba is valid because the airspace above it (muḥādhāt) constitutes the qibla, but it is disliked out of reverence for the Kaaba's sanctity.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Prayer Validity When Follower is Closer to the Kaaba than Imam
Ruling on the validity of prayer when followers are closer to the Kaaba than the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a follower's prayer in the Sacred Mosque is valid when closer to the Kaaba than the imam, and apply the ruling to different positions.

Core Idea
A follower's prayer is invalid only if he is on the imam's side and closer to the Kaaba.

This lesson examines a unique scenario in the Masjid al-Haram where followers pray around the Kaaba. The key principle is that the follower must not be ahead of the imam. We will see how proximity to the Kaaba relative to the imam interacts with being on the same side, and how this affects the validity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying in congregation with the imam in the Sacred Mosque. The ruling is that the prayer is generally valid except when the follower is on the imam's side and closer to the Kaaba.
2
Understand the key condition: side and proximity
Validity depends on whether the follower is on the same side as the imam. If on the same side and closer to Kaaba, then ahead, invalid. If on a different side, closer is not ahead, so valid.
Being closer to the Qibla on the imam's side constitutes being ahead.
3
Visualize the scenario
The text includes a diagram: only the follower directly in front of the imam and closer to the Kaaba is invalid; all others are valid.
The diagram shows followers around the Kaaba with the imam at one side.
4
State the principle
The underlying principle: a follower must not be ahead of the imam. In circular prayers, 'ahead' is defined by being on the same side and closer to the Qibla.
This is an exception to the general rule that the follower must be behind the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۴۵۰ (۵) واذا صلى الامام في المسجد الحرام تحلق الناس حول الكعبة وصلوا بصلوة الامام فمن كان منهم اقرب الى الكعبة من الامام جازت صلوته اذا لم يكن في جانب الامام
اگر مسجد حرام میں نماز پڑھائے اور سب لوگ کعبہ کے ارد گر د حلقہ بنائے اور امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تو جوان میں سے کعبہ سے زیادہ قریب ہو امام سے بھی تو اس کی نماز جائز ہے جب کہ امام کی جانب نہ ہو۔
امام کی جانب جو لوگ ہو اور امام سے بھی زیادہ بیت اللہ کے قریب ہو جائے تو امام کی جانب امام سے بھی آگے ہو جائے ئیں گے اس لئے اس آدمی کی نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ اور جو لوگ امام کی جانب نہیں ہیں دوسری جانب ہیں وہ لوگ اگر کعبہ کے زیادہ قریب ہو گئے تو چونکہ وہ امام کی جانب نہیں ہیں اس لئے امام سے آگے نہیں ہوئے اس لئے ان کی نماز ہو جائے گی۔
امام سے آگے مقتدی ہو جائے تو اس کی نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی ورنہ ہو جائے گی۔ نقشہ اس طرح ہے۔ (بیت اللہ کے اردگرد نماز پڑھنے کا نقشہ )

And if the imam prays in the Sacred Mosque, and people gather around the Kaaba and pray with the imam's prayer, then whoever among them is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, his prayer is valid if he is not on the side of the imam. If he leads prayer in the Masjid al-Haram and all people form a circle around the Kaaba and pray with the imam, then whoever among them is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, his prayer is permissible, provided he is not on the imam's side. Those who are on the imam's side and are closer to the Kaaba than the imam will become ahead of the imam on his side, therefore that person's prayer will not be valid. And those who are not on the imam's side but on the other side, if they become closer to the Kaaba, since they are not on the imam's side, they have not become ahead of the imam, so their prayer will be valid. If the follower becomes ahead of the imam, his prayer is not valid; otherwise it will be valid. The diagram is as follows: ... His prayer will not be valid; the rest will be valid.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on prayer, specifically about following the imam in the Sacred Mosque. It explains that if people pray around the Kaaba, their proximity to the Kaaba relative to the imam matters only if they are on the same side as the imam. Being closer to the Kaaba on the imam's side makes the follower ahead of the imam, which invalidates the prayer. On other sides, being closer does not put them ahead, so the prayer is valid. The core Hanafi principle here is that the follower must not be ahead of the imam in prayer. The text uses a diagram to illustrate, showing that only the follower directly in front of the imam and closer to the Kaaba is invalid; all others are valid.

Key Terms
امام (imam): The leader of congregational prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower praying behind the imam.
جانب (janib): Side or direction relative to the imam; here it specifically refers to being aligned with the imam's direction (same side of the Kaaba).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Masjid al-Haram, if followers pray around the Kaaba and some are closer to the Kaaba than the imam, what condition determines whether their prayer is valid?
A) Being closer always invalidates.
B) Being on the imam's side and closer invalidates.
C) Only if they are behind the imam.
D) All prayers are valid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a follower's prayer in a circular prayer around the Kaaba depends on whether he is on the imam's side and closer to the Kaaba, which constitutes being ahead.
